٤ - القيام بالنفس والإرادة وغيرها، لكنّها واجبة القيام به تعالی (۱)، هذا خُلْفٌ (۲). قوله: (لكنها واجبة القيام به) :أي فاستحال كونه صفة ، فاستحال قيامه بالمحل، فثبت كونه قائما بنفسه الشنواني . قوله: (هذا خلف) بفتح الخاء؛ أي: مرمي به وراء الظهر. أو بضمها؛ أي: كذب وباطل. الأمير . قوله: (لوجوب وجوده وقدمه) أي وجوبهما مستلزم للاستغناء عن المخصص، لأنه لو احتاج إليه لكان حادثا ، فينافي ما تقدم من وجوب الوجود والقدم . وهذا استدلال على الجزء الثاني من جزئي مفهوم القيام بالنفس ببرهان اقتراني تقريره الله تعالى واجب له الوجود والقدم والبقاء، وكل من وجب له ذلك فهو مُستغن عن المخصص ، يُنتج : الله مستغن عن المخصص . ويصح أن يكون إشارة إلى قياس استثنائي، تقريره : لو لم يستغن عن المخصص لما وجبَ وجوده وقدمه وبقاؤه، لكنه تعالى وجب وجوده وقدمه وبقاؤه، ينتج: أنه تعالى مستغن عن المخصص ، وبيان الملازمة: أن كل موجود يفتقر إلى المخصص حادث ، ودليل الاستثنائية ما مر ، لكنه تعالى وجب وجوده وقدمه وبقاؤه الشنواني . البحث في صفة قيام الله تعالى بنفسه يتعلق بها من جهتين، الأولى: بيان معنى قيامه بنفسه ، والثانية : الدليل على أنه يجب الله تعالى القيام بنفسه. أما معنی قیامه بنفسه فعدم افتقاره جل شأنه إلى المحل أو المخصص ، والمراد بالمحل هنا الذَّاتُ ، وليس المراد به في هذا الموضع المكان ؛ لأن عدم افتقاره إلى المكان مفهوم مخالفته تعالى للحوادث على ما سبق، فالمعنى أنه سبحانه مستغن عن ذات يقوم بها، ويلزم من ذلك أن يكون ذاتا لا صفةً، لأنَّ الصَّفة لا بد أن تقوم بمحل، أي: ذات تتصف بها. والمراد بالمُخصّص - بكسر الصاد - الفاعل والموجد، أي: أنه تعالى مستغن عن موجد يوجده ، ويلزم من ذلك أن يكون قديما لا حادثاً ، ومن هذا التقرير تفهم أن معنى قيامه بنفسه يتضمن شيئين، الأول: عدم احتياجه إلى المحل ، والثاني: عدم احتياجه إلى الموجد ، وتفهم أيضا أن صفة القدم كان يمكن أن يستغنى بها عن عدم الاحتياج إلى الموجد ؛ لأنه لا يحتاج إلى الموجد إلَّا الحادث، لكن علماء هذا الفن لا يكتفون بدلالة الالتزام لشدة خطر الجهل في موضوعاتِ هذا العلم على ما علمت مما سبق . وأما الدليل على وجوب قيامه تعالى بنفسه فيحتاج إلى دليلين: أحدهما: يثبت عدم احتياجه إلى المحل، والثاني: يثبت عدم احتياجه إلى المخصص وهو الفاعل والموجد على ما علمت. والدليل على عدم احتياجه إلى المحل: أنه لو افتقر إلى محل يقوم به لكان صفة، ولو كان صفةٌ لم يصح اتصافه بشيء من صفات المعاني والمعنوية، وهو سبحانه واجب الاتصاف بكل صفة من صفات المعاني والمعنوية ، أما أنه سبحانه واجب الاتصاف بكل صفة من صفات المعاني والمعنوية ، فلما يُذكر من الأدلة كل صفة منها، وأما دليل الملازمة في مع قولنا : «لو كان صفة لم يصح اتصافه بشيء من ... إلخ» ، فدليلها ما ثبت من كون الصفة لا توصف ، إذ لو قبلت الصفةُ صفةٌ أخرى لزم ألا تخلو عنها أو عن مثلها أو عن ضدها، ويلزم في الصفة الأخرى ، وهلم جرا ، ويتسلسل أو يدور . وأما دليل الملازمة في قولنا: لو افتقر إلى محل ، أي : ذات ـ على ما علمت ـ لكان صفة» ، فأنه لا يقوم بالذات إلّا صفاتُها ، ومتى ثبت اتصافه سبحانه بصفات المعاني والمعنوية ، بطل كونه صفةٌ ، ومتى بطل كونه صفةٌ بطل كونه مفتقرًا إلى محلّ، ومتى بطل كونه مفتقرا إلى محلّ ثبت نقيضُه ، وهو عدم افتقاره إلى المحل ، وهو المطلوب. وأما الدليل على عدم افتقاره إلى مخصص ، أي : موجد يوجده : فأنه لو افتقر إلى المخصص لكان حادثاً ، ولكنه ليس بحادث ، فليس مفتقرا إلى المخصص. فأما دليل الاستثنائية، وهي قولنا لكنه ليس بحادث ، فهو ما تقدم من دليل القدم، وإذا بطل كونه حادثا بطل ما أدى إليه ، وهو أنه محتاج إلى مخصص، وإذا بطل ذلك ثبت نقيضه وهو عدم احتياجه إلى المخصص، وهو المطلوب. محي.
4 - Self-subsistence, will, and others, but they are necessarily subsisting in Him, exalted is He (1), this is a contradiction (2). His statement: (but they are necessarily subsisting in Him) means: so it is impossible for it to be an attribute, so its subsistence in a substrate is impossible, so it is established that it is self-subsistent. [al-Shanwani]. His statement: (this is khalaf) with fath of the kha': i.e., cast behind the back. Or with damm: i.e., false and invalid. [al-Amir]. His statement: (due to the necessity of His existence and pre-eternity) means: their necessity entails independence from the specifier, because if He needed it He would be originated, contradicting what preceded of the necessity of existence and pre-eternity. This is a proof for the second part of the two parts of the concept of self-subsistence by a conjunctive syllogism: God, exalted, has necessary existence, pre-eternity, and everlastingness, and whoever has that is independent of the specifier; conclusion: God is independent of the specifier. And it is correct that it is an indication of an exceptional syllogism: if He were not independent of the specifier, His existence, pre-eternity, and everlastingness would not be necessary, but He, exalted, has necessary existence, pre-eternity, and everlastingness; conclusion: He, exalted, is independent of the specifier. And the explanation of the implication: every existent that depends on the specifier is originated; the proof of the exceptional is what has passed, but He, exalted, has necessary existence, pre-eternity, and everlastingness. [al-Shanwani]. The investigation into the attribute of God's self-subsistence concerns two aspects: first, the explanation of the meaning of His self-subsistence; second, the proof that God, exalted, must be self-subsistent. As for the meaning of His self-subsistence: it is His lack of need, glory be to Him, for a substrate or a specifier. What is meant by 'substrate' here is the essence (dhat), not place (makan) in this context, because His lack of need for place is the concept of His dissimilarity to originated things as previously. So the meaning is that He, glorified, is independent of an essence in which He subsists, and it follows from that that He is an essence, not an attribute, because an attribute must subsist in a substrate, i.e., an essence qualified by it. What is meant by 'specifier' (mukhassis) — with kasr of the sad — is the agent and bringer into existence, i.e., He, exalted, is independent of a bringer into existence that brings Him into existence, and it follows from that that He is pre-eternal, not originated. From this presentation you understand that the meaning of His self-subsistence includes two things: first, His lack of need for a substrate; second, His lack of need for a bringer into existence. And you also understand that the attribute of pre-eternity could suffice for lack of need for a bringer into existence, because nothing needs a bringer into existence except the originated, but the scholars of this art are not satisfied with the implicative indication due to the severity of the danger of ignorance in the subjects of this science, as you have learned from what preceded. As for the proof of the necessity of His self-subsistence, it requires two proofs: one establishes His lack of need for a substrate, and the second establishes His lack of need for a specifier, which is the agent and bringer into existence as you have learned. The proof of His lack of need for a substrate: if He depended on a substrate in which to subsist, He would be an attribute; and if He were an attribute, it would not be correct for Him to be qualified by any of the attributes of meanings (sifat al-ma'ani) and the meaningful (al-ma'nawiyya), but He, glorified, necessarily qualifies with every attribute of meanings and the meaningful. As for that He, glorified, necessarily qualifies with every attribute of meanings and the meaningful, it is according to the proofs that will be mentioned for each attribute. As for the proof of the implication in our statement 'if He were an attribute, it would not be correct for Him to be qualified by any... etc.', its proof is what is established that the attribute is not qualified, because if an attribute accepted another attribute, it would necessarily not be free of it or its like or its opposite, and the same would follow for the other attribute, and so on, leading to infinite regress or circularity. As for the proof of the implication in our statement 'if He depended on a substrate, i.e., an essence — as you have learned — He would be an attribute', it is that nothing subsists in an essence except its attributes. And when His qualification, glorified, with attributes of meanings and the meaningful is established, His being an attribute is invalidated; and when His being an attribute is invalidated, His being dependent on a substrate is invalidated; and when His being dependent on a substrate is invalidated, its opposite is established, which is His lack of dependence on a substrate; that is what is sought. As for the proof of His lack of need for a specifier, i.e., a bringer into existence that brings Him into existence: if He depended on the specifier, He would be originated, but He is not originated, so He is not dependent on the specifier. As for the proof of the exception, which is our statement 'but He is not originated', it is what preceded from the proof of pre-eternity. And when His being originated is invalidated, what it leads to is invalidated, namely that He is in need of a specifier; and when that is invalidated, its opposite is established, which is His lack of need for the specifier; that is what is sought. [Muhi].
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the fourth negative attribute of Allah: al-qiyam bi al-nafs (self-subsistence). The commentator begins by citing the matn line that states self-subsistence, will, and other attributes are necessarily subsisting in Allah, and that a contradiction would arise otherwise. He then explains the matn notes: first, that if the attributes were not necessarily subsisting in Him, they would be impossible as attributes, and the only alternative is that they are self-subsistent attributes. Second, he glosses 'khalaf' as either 'cast away' or 'false'. Third, he explains the proof from the necessity of existence and pre-eternity: because Allah's existence and pre-eternity are necessary, He must be independent of any specifier (mukhassis), since needing a specifier would imply origination. This is presented as both a conjunctive syllogism and an exceptional syllogism. Next, the commentator enters the main investigation (bahth), organizing it into two aspects: the meaning of self-subsistence and the proof that it is necessary for Allah. The meaning is that Allah does not need a substrate (mahl) — where 'substrate' means an essence (dhat), not a place, as the latter is already negated by tanzih — and does not need a specifier (mukhassis) meaning a creator. From this, two implications follow: without a substrate, Allah is an essence not an attribute; without a specifier, He is pre-eternal not originated. The commentator notes that the attribute of pre-eternity alone could imply independence from a creator by implication (dalalat al-iltizam), but scholars do not rely on that due to the risk of error. Then he presents the two proofs. The first proof against needing a substrate is a conditional argument: if Allah depended on a substrate, He would be an attribute; if He were an attribute, He could not be qualified with the attributes of meanings (sifat al-ma'ani) and the meaningful (al-ma'nawiyya), which He necessarily is. The impossibility of an attribute being qualified is argued through the threat of infinite regress or circularity. The second proof against needing a specifier is simple: if He needed a specifier, He would be originated, but He is not originated (proved by the earlier proof of pre-eternity). The conclusion of each is the negation of dependence, establishing self-subsistence.

The Linguistic Meaning of al-Wahdaniyya (Oneness)
Commentator explains the linguistic derivation and meaning of wahdaniyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the term al-wahdaniyya is derived from al-wahda and why its form conveys intensification, as well as the key linguistic debate about its structure.

Core Idea
Al-wahdaniyya is an intensive form emphasizing absolute, indivisible oneness, not a mere relation.

The fifth negative attribute of Allah is al-wahdaniyya (Oneness). Before we explore its theological significance, the commentator begins by unpacking the Arabic term itself. Understanding the linguistic structure of 'wahdaniyya' helps us grasp why this attribute is fundamental to tawhid. The following passage explains its derivation and introduces a scholarly discussion about its precise meaning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once without pausing on details. Then read the literal translation to get a sense of the argument.
The passage is part of a larger discussion; we only have the opening segment.
2
Understand the derivation
Note that 'wahdaniyya' is derived from 'al-wahda' (unity) with the relative ya (ya al-nisba). The addition of alif and nun before the ya serves to intensify the meaning.
The commentator gives examples: 'ruqbani' (neck) and 'shu'rani' (hair) to illustrate this pattern.
3
Identify the debate
Some scholars argue that the ya cannot be for relation because the purpose is to affirm unity itself, not something related to unity. Think about why this distinction matters for the attribute of Oneness.
The passage cuts off mid-sentence, indicating the debate continues. Reflect on what might come next.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٥ - الوحدانية ] والصفة الخامسة من الصفات السَّلبيَّة الواجبة له تعالى (وَحْدَانِيَّة)(۱) اعلم أوَّلاً : أنَّ الوَحْدانية - بفتح الواو وسكون الحاء - نسبة إلى الوحدة، فهذه «الياء» التي فيها ياء النسبة ، وقد زيدت الألف والنون قبل «الياء» لإفادة المبالغة، كما زيدت في «رقباني» و«شعراني» وهما منسوبان إلى (الرقبة) و(الشعر). وقيل: لا يصح كون «الياء» للنسبة ، لأنَّ المراد ثبوت الوحدة نفسها ، لا ثبوت شيء منسوب إليها ، وصاحب هذا القيل =
[5 - Oneness] And the fifth attribute of the negative attributes necessarily attributed to Him, exalted, is oneness (wahdaniyya)(1). Know, first, that al-wahdaniyya — with fatha on the waw and sukun on the ha — is a relative noun derived from unity (al-wahda). So this 'ya' in it is the ya of relation, and the alif and nun have been added before the 'ya' to convey intensification (mubalagha), just as they are added in 'ruqbani' and 'shu'rani', which are related to 'al-ruqba' (the neck) and 'al-sha'r' (hair). And it is said that it is not correct for the 'ya' to be for relation, because what is intended is the affirmation of unity itself, not the affirmation of something related to it. And the proponent of this view =
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage introduces the fifth negative attribute, al-wahdaniyya (Oneness). The commentator begins by citing the matn line that places it as the fifth negative attribute necessarily attributed to Allah. Then he provides a linguistic analysis of the term. He explains that 'wahdaniyya' is derived from 'al-wahda' (unity) using the relative ya (ya' al-nisba). The form includes an extra alif and nun before the ya, which indicates intensification (mubalagha). He gives examples: 'ruqbani' (related to the neck) and 'shu'rani' (related to hair), where the alif and nun are added for emphasis. Then he mentions that some scholars object to the ya being a relative suffix, arguing that the purpose is to affirm unity itself, not something related to unity. The passage cuts off midsentence, indicating the debate continues on the next page.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that wahdaniyya simply means 'one in number' or that it is a relative quality like 'redness'.
Correction: The intensive form shows that wahdaniyya means absolute, indivisible oneness that admits no multiplicity, not a mere numerical attribute.

Checkpoint
What linguistic device is used in the word 'wahdaniyya' to emphasize oneness?
A) The addition of alif and nun before the ya of relation
B) The repetition of the root letters
C) The feminine ending 'a'
D) The use of a passive participle

Key Takeaway
Al-wahdaniyya derives from unity (al-wahda) with an intensive form, emphasizing that Allah's oneness is absolute and not a mere relational quality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

What would change if you truly lived as if nothing deserves your ultimate devotion except the One who is absolutely one?
?
The scholars debated whether the 'ya' in الوحدانية is for relation or for something else. This shows how seriously they took every word about Allah. When was the last time you examined a word or belief about Allah with such care? Could your casual understanding of tawhid be hiding a deeper indifference?

If Allah's oneness is absolute and not just a numerical property, then nothing else can share in His exclusive right to be worshipped. What are you currently treating as important alongside Allah? Name one attachment you need to break because it competes with the reality of His الوحدانية.

The Definition of al-Wahdaniyya and the Five Types of Multiplicity Negated
Defines wahdaniyya as negation of multiplicity and enumerates five kumum negated.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that al-wahdaniyya (Allah's Oneness) is defined as the negation of multiplicity in three domains—essence, attributes, and acts—and you will be able to identify the five specific types of 'quantity' (kumum) that are negated by each type of unity.

Core Idea
Allah's Oneness negates five forms of multiplicity: in essence, attributes, and acts.

This passage from the Jawharat al-Tawhid commentary lays the conceptual foundation for understanding the divine attribute of wahdaniyya. It is not merely a statement that Allah is one, but a precise negation of any and all multiplicity—whether in His essence, His attributes, or His acts. The author, Imam al-Laqqani, unpacks this by introducing five categories of 'quantity' (kum) that are denied of Allah, providing a clear and comprehensive framework for tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two aspects
The passage starts by stating that wahdaniyya is studied from two angles: explaining its meaning and proving it. Note these two aspects as they organize the discussion.
2
Grasp the definition of wahdaniyya
Understand that the core meaning is 'negation of multiplicity' (nafy al-ta'addud) applied to three domains: essence, attributes, and acts.
3
Learn the five types of quantity (kumum)
List each of the five kumum: connected/disconnected in essence, connected/disconnected in attributes, and disconnected in acts. Understand what each negates.
Notice that 'connected' refers to internal composition, while 'disconnected' refers to external plurality.
4
Connect the types to the three unities
See how unity of essence negates the first two quantities, unity of attributes negates the next two, and unity of acts negates the last one.
5
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this detailed negation is necessary for a proper understanding of tawhid and how it protects against various forms of shirk.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثمَّ اعلم أن البحث في صفة الوحدانية يتعلق بها من جهتين، الجهة الأولى: في بيان معنى الوحدانية وما يرتبط به والجهة الثانية في إقامة الدليل على وجوب الوحدانية لله. أما الكلام فيما يتعلق بمعنى الوحدانية وما يتصل به فنقول : معنى الوحدانية الواجبة له تعالى نفي التَّعدد في ذاته وفي صفاته وفي أفعاله ، وقد اشتهر أنَّ الوحدانية تنفي كُمُومًا خمسةً وهي: الكم المتصل في الذات، ومعناه: أنّ ذاته مركبة من أجزاء. والكمُّ المنفصل في الذات أيضاً، ومعناه: تعدد ذات الواجب بحيث يكون هناك إله ثانٍ ، أو أكثر. والكم المتصل في الصفات، ومعناه: تعدد الصفات: وهو في صفاته تعالى بأن يكون له صفتان من جنس واحد، كقدرتين وإرادتين وعلمين. والكمُّ المنفصل في الصفات، ومعناه: أن يكون لغيره صفةٌ تُشبه صفته؛ كأن يكون لأحدٍ قدرة يُوجد بها ويُعدم كقدرة الله تعالى، أو يكون لأحدٍ إرادة تخصص الممكن ببعض ما يجوز عليه ، أو علم محيط بجميع الأشياء وهكذا. والكمُّ المنفصل في الأفعال ، ومعناه : أن يكون لغيره تعالى فعل من الأفعال على وجه الإيجاد. فوحدة الذات الواجبة له تعالى معناها: أنه ليس جسما مركبا يقبل الانقسام، وأنه ليس هناك إله آخر غيره، ووحدة الأفعال معناها: أنه ليس لأحدٍ فعل كفعله ، وبعبارة أخرى: أنَّ وَحدة الذات تنفي عنه الكم المتصل والكمّ المنفصل في الذات ، ووحدة الصفات تنفي عنه الكمّ المتصل والكم المنفصل في الصفات ، ووحدة الأفعال تنفي عنه الكم المنفصل في الأفعال.
Then know that the research in the attribute of al-wahdaniyya pertains to it from two aspects: the first aspect is explaining the meaning of al-wahdaniyya and what is connected to it, and the second aspect is establishing the proof for the obligation of al-wahdaniyya for Allah. As for the discussion regarding the meaning of al-wahdaniyya and what is connected to it, we say: the meaning of al-wahdaniyya obligatory for Him, exalted is He, is the negation of multiplicity in His essence, in His attributes, and in His acts. And it is well-known that al-wahdaniyya negates five quantities (kumum): the connected quantity in the essence, and its meaning is that His essence is composed of parts. And the disconnected quantity in the essence also, and its meaning is the multiplicity of the essence of the Necessary such that there is a second god or more. And the connected quantity in the attributes, and its meaning is the multiplicity of attributes: which is in His attributes, exalted is He, that He should have two attributes of one kind, like two powers, two wills, and two knowledges. And the disconnected quantity in the attributes, and its meaning is that someone other than Him should have an attribute resembling His attribute; such as someone having a power by which he brings into existence and annihilates like the power of Allah Most High, or someone having a will that particularizes the possible with some of what is permissible for it, or an encompassing knowledge of all things, and so on. And the disconnected quantity in the acts, and its meaning is that someone other than Him, exalted is He, should do an act of the acts in the manner of origination. So the unity of the essence obligatory for Him, exalted is He, means that He is not a composite body accepting division, and that there is no other god besides Him. And the unity of the acts means that no one has an act like His act. In other words, the unity of the essence negates from Him the connected quantity and the disconnected quantity in the essence, and the unity of the attributes negates from Him the connected quantity and the disconnected quantity in the attributes, and the unity of the acts negates from Him the disconnected quantity in the acts.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage defines the meaning of the divine attribute of wahdaniyya (Oneness). It begins by stating that the study of this attribute has two aspects: (1) explaining its meaning and related matters, and (2) proving that it is necessary for Allah. The author then focuses on the first aspect. He defines wahdaniyya as the negation of multiplicity (nafy al-ta'addud) in Allah's essence, attributes, and acts. This negation is then detailed through five types of 'quantity' (kum, pl. kumum) that are negated. The five types are: 1) Connected quantity in the essence: meaning that the essence is not composed of parts (i.e., not a body). 2) Disconnected quantity in the essence: meaning there is no second god or more. 3) Connected quantity in the attributes: meaning there are not two attributes of the same kind (e.g., two powers). 4) Disconnected quantity in the attributes: meaning no creature has an attribute truly resembling Allah's attribute (like creative power or all-encompassing knowledge). 5) Disconnected quantity in the acts: meaning no one else originates an act as Allah does. The passage concludes by summarizing: unity of essence negates types 1 and 2, unity of attributes negates types 3 and 4, and unity of acts negates type 5.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Wahdaniyya only means there is one God, and it does not address plurality in attributes or acts.
Correction: Wahdaniyya explicitly negates multiplicity in all three domains: essence, attributes, and acts, as demonstrated by the five types of quantity.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type of quantity is negated by the unity of acts (wahdat al-af'al)?
A) The connected quantity in the attributes
B) The disconnected quantity in the essence
C) The disconnected quantity in the acts
D) The connected quantity in the essence

Key Takeaway
Al-wahdaniyya is the negation of all five types of multiplicity: compositional parts, other gods, duplicate attributes, shared perfect attributes, and independent creative acts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
When you look at your attachments to wealth, status, or relationships, do they ever function as hidden 'gods' in your heart? How does the negation of disconnected quantity in essence challenge you to recenter your worship on Allah alone?
?
Have you ever felt pride in your accomplishments as if you originated them yourself? How does the unity of acts force you to reconsider your role in every outcome? What concrete step will you take today to acknowledge Allah's exclusive role in creation?

The Three Categories of Divine Oneness
Enumeration of the three categories of divine oneness with definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three meanings of divine oneness: oneness of essence as incompositeness, oneness of attributes as no duplicate traits, and oneness of actions as exclusive origination.

Core Idea
Divine oneness means no parts, no duplicate attributes, and no creator but Allah.

This passage from the commentary distinguishes three distinct senses in which we say Allah is one. Each meaning addresses a different potential misunderstanding about Allah's nature and actions. The author links them to other parts of the matn.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the references to later lines in the matn.
2
Identify the three categories
The passage presents three meanings of oneness: essence, attributes, and actions. Find each one and notice how the author defines it.
3
Reflect on the sources of these meanings
The author derives the first meaning (essence) from the attribute of being unlike originated things. The other two are linked to later discussions. Think about why these distinctions matter.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم الإلهيات واعلم أنَّ وحدة الذات بمعنى: عدم التركيب من أجزاء مستفادة من صفة المخالفة للحوادث ، وأن وحدة الصفات بمعنى: أنه ليس له سبحانه صفتان من جنس واحد قد أفردها المصنف بالذكر فيما يأتي حيث قال: (وَوَحْدَةٌ أَوْجِبْ لَهَا ... إلخ) وأن وحدة الأفعال بمعنى: أنه ليس لغيره سبحانه فعل مِن الأفعال على وجه الإيجاد، قد أفردها المصنف أيضا بالذكر فيما يأتي في مبحث خلق الأفعال حيث قال : وخَالقٌ لعبدِه ومَا عَمِل ... إلخ) فبقي مما تدل عليه الوحدانية ولم يذكر في غير هذا الموضع أمران : وحدة الذات، بمعنى: أنه ليس هناك : ذات أخرى تشبه ذاته ، ووحدة الصفات، بمعنى أنه ليس لغيره صفة تشبه صفته .
The section of divine matters. And know that oneness of essence means: absence of composition from parts derived from the attribute of being unlike originated things. And that oneness of attributes means: that He, exalted, does not have two attributes of the same genus, which the author has singled out for mention later where he said: 'And oneness oblige for it... etc.' And that oneness of actions means: that no other than Him, exalted, has any act in the manner of origination, which the author also singled out for mention later in the topic of creation of actions where he said: 'And Creator of His servant and what he did... etc.' So what remains of what oneness indicates and has not been mentioned elsewhere are two matters: oneness of essence, meaning: that there is no other essence that resembles His essence, and oneness of attributes, meaning: that there is no other attribute that resembles His attribute.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage classifies the meanings of divine oneness (al-waḥdāniyya) into three categories: oneness of essence, oneness of attributes, and oneness of actions. For each, a specific meaning is given:
1. Oneness of essence means that the divine essence is not composed of parts, and this is derived from the attribute of being unlike originated things (mukhālafa lil-ḥawādith).
2. Oneness of attributes means that God does not have two attributes of the same kind (e.g., two powers or two knowledges). The author alludes to a later line: 'وَوَحْدَةٌ أَوْجِبْ لَهَا' (And oneness, oblige for it...).
3. Oneness of actions means that no one other than God performs acts in the sense of bringing into existence. The author refers to a later discussion on the creation of actions.
After listing these three, the passage notes that two other aspects remain, which have not been mentioned here: (A) oneness of essence meaning that there is no other essence like His essence, and (B) oneness of attributes meaning that there is no other attribute like His attribute. Thus, oneness implies both internal incompositeness and external incomparability.

Key Terms
وحدة الذات
وحدة الصفات
وحدة الأفعال
المخالفة للحوادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think 'oneness of attributes' means Allah has only one attribute, or that oneness of essence means simply that Allah is one in number.
Correction: Oneness of attributes means no two attributes of the same kind exist in Allah (e.g., not two knowledges), not that He has only one attribute. Oneness of essence means not composed of parts, not merely numerical oneness.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does 'oneness of essence' (وحدة الذات) mean?
A) Allah is one in number.
B) Absence of composition from parts.
C) No other essence like His.
D) He has no attributes.

Key Takeaway
Divine oneness is understood in three specific ways: essence is not composed, attributes have no duplicates, and actions are exclusively His.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on the fact that Allah's essence has no parts, does it make you realize that your attempts to compartmentalize Him into separate 'spaces' of your life are actually a form of subtle deification of your own limited understanding? How can you begin to address Him as the simple, undivided One in your daily prayers?
?
If no one but Allah truly originates any action, what does that mean for your pride in your own achievements or your despair over your failures? Can you sincerely say that you attribute every breath and every deed solely to Him, or do you still secretly claim some share of creation?
?
Knowing that Allah has no duplicate attributes—that His mercy, power, and knowledge are each absolutely unique—does your worship become more focused on the singularity of His being? Or do you still fall into comparing His attributes to human qualities, and if so, what will you do to correct that today?

The Two Remaining Aspects of Oneness
Addition of two final aspects of divine oneness: no peer in essence and no peer in attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two additional aspects of divine oneness: that no essence resembles Allah's essence and no attribute resembles His attribute.

Core Idea
Oneness also means Allah is absolutely unique—no like in essence or attributes.

After establishing the first three meanings, the commentator adds two more aspects of oneness that are covered elsewhere in the matn. These emphasize Allah's incomparability beyond just composition and exclusivity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how the author introduces these as 'what remains'.
These two aspects are distinct from the earlier three.
2
Identify the two aspects
The passage presents two matters: oneness of essence meaning no other essence like His, and oneness of attributes meaning no other attribute like His. Write them down.
3
Distinguish from the earlier meanings
Earlier, oneness of essence meant 'not composed'; here it means 'no like'. Similarly, earlier oneness of attributes meant 'no duplicate genus'; here it means 'no similar attribute'. Compare and contrast.
This establishes a fuller understanding of tawheed.

Divine Attributes in the State of Transcendence
Introduces divine transcendence and conditional affirmation of attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that divine transcendence does not negate God's attributes but rather affirms them while denying any imperfection.

Core Idea
Transcendence affirms attributes while denying all deficiency.

This lesson unpacks a crucial section from the Jawharah that clarifies the proper belief about God's attributes. The author emphasizes that when we affirm attributes for Allah, we must do so while affirming His absolute transcendence—free from any opposite or deficiency. Understanding this interplay is foundational to all subsequent discussions of God's nature.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the compact style: the passage is a single sentence with glosses.
2
Understand key terms
Identify the two key categories: التنزيهات (transcendent affirmations) and السلوب (negations). Note that 'transcendence' here means being free from any opposite or something that accompanies deficiency.
The author glosses 'مُنَزَّه' as in a state of necessary transcendence.
3
Grasp the core teaching
The passage states that God necessarily has the attributes mentioned earlier, but this is always in a state of transcendence. That means we affirm attributes while denying any imperfection. This is the balanced position between negation (ta'til) and anthropomorphism (tashbih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو تفصيل لبابِ التَّنزيهاتِ والسُّلوبِ ومما يجب اعتقاده أنَّه تعالى وجبت له الصّفاتُ المذكورة حال كونه (مُنَزَّها) أي: في حال وجوب تنزهه عن ضدّ وما معه (أَوْصَافهُ) أي: صِفاته
And it is a detailing of the chapter of transcendent affirmations and negations. And among what must be believed is that He, exalted, necessarily has the aforementioned attributes while being (transcendent), that is, in a state of necessary transcendence from opposite and what accompanies it; (His attributes) meaning His attributes.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This short passage introduces a new section titled 'تفصيل باب التنزيهات والسلوب' (Detailing the Chapter of Transcendent Affirmations and Negations). It states that it is obligatory to believe that God, exalted, possesses the previously mentioned attributes while being in a state of transcendence (munazzah). The term 'transcendence' here means that God is absolutely free from any opposite (ḍidd) or anything that accompanies deficiency. The parenthetical gloss clarifies that 'His attributes' (awṣāfuhu) refer to His attributes (ṣifātuhu). This sets the stage for discussing God's attributes in conjunction with His transcendence, ensuring that attributes are affirmed without compromising divine incomparability.

Key Terms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that divine transcendence means God has no attributes at all, or that attributes are mere negations.
Correction: The passage shows that transcendence is a condition of the attributes; attributes are affirmed, but in a way that transcends any defect. It is not a denial of attributes but a denial of imperfection.

Key Takeaway
God's attributes are affirmed while maintaining His absolute transcendence from any flaw.

The Twofold Meaning of 'Suniyyah'
The commentator explains the meaning of 'suniyyah' applied to God's attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the twofold interpretation of the divine attribute 'suniyyah' as either 'lofty' or 'luminous' and the Ash'ari caution against literal anthropomorphism.

Core Idea
'Suniyyah' illuminates two facets of divine attributes: loftiness and guidance, not literal light.

This lesson unpacks the meaning of the term 'suniyyah' that the poet uses to describe God's attributes. The commentator offers two possible derivations from Arabic roots, each carrying a distinct nuance. By examining these, we see how Ash'ari theology balances affirmation of divine attributes with transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage from the matn and the commentator's footnote. Then read the English translation to grasp the two proposed meanings.
Pay attention to the two roots mentioned: al-sana' (with long alif) and al-sana (shortened).
2
Identify the two meanings
Note that 'suniyyah' can mean 'lofty' (from al-sana') or 'luminous/light-like' (from al-sana). See how the commentator supports the latter with the Quranic verse about lightning.
3
Understand the theological caution
The commentator warns against taking the 'light' meaning literally, because light is an accident and cannot subsist in an eternal attribute. The comparison is metaphorical, indicating guidance.
This reflects the Ash'ari principle of tanzih (transcendence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم الإلهيات
مطلقا (سَنِيَّه) أي: كالنُّور ، بجامع الاهتداء، أو معناه: رفيعة(۱)
(1) يريد له أن يقول : إِنَّ (سنية) في كلام المصنف فَعِيلَة ، ويجوز أن يكون مأخذها السَنَاء بالمد ـ وهو الرّفْعَة، فيكون المعنى: أن صفاته الرفيعة، أو يكون مأخذها السَنَا بالقصر ـ وهو الضوء والنور ، ومنه قوله سبحانه: ﴿يَكَادُ سَنَا بَرْقِهِ يَذْهَبُ بِالْأَبْصَرِ﴾ [النور: ٤٣] ويكون المعنى على تشبيه صفاته بالضوء، الا بمعنى أن صفاته قام بها النور؛ لأن النور عرض يستحيل قيامه بالصفة قديمة كانت أو حادثة ] محي الدين والشنواني.
Section of Divine Matters. Absolutely, (suniyyah) meaning: like light, due to the commonality of guidance, or its meaning is lofty (1). (1) He intends to say: Indeed, (suniyyah) in the author's speech is fa'ilah, and it is permissible that its derivation is from al-sana' with alif (elongation) which is highness, so the meaning is: His exalted attributes, or its derivation is from al-sana with shortening which is light and illumination, and from it is His statement, the Most High: 'The lightning of His cloud almost takes away the eyesight' [Surah al-Nur: 43], and the meaning would be likening His attributes to light, except with the meaning that His attributes are characterized by light; because light is an accident and it is impossible for it to subsist in the attribute whether ancient or originated. By Muhyi al-Din and al-Shanwani.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage explains the word 'suniyyah' which appears in the matn (poem) as a description of the divine attributes. The commentator notes that 'suniyyah' can be interpreted in two ways. First, from the root 'sana' with elongation (al-sana') meaning 'highness' or 'loftiness', thus the attributes are described as 'lofty'. Second, from the root 'sana' with shortening (al-sana) meaning 'light' or 'illumination', thus likening the attributes to light in guiding. The author cites the Quranic verse (24:43) that uses 'sana' for lightning. However, the commentator adds a caution: the comparison is not literal, because light is an accident and cannot be an attribute of the eternal God. Rather, the meaning is that the attributes are like light in their guidance, not that they are light itself. This is a typical Ash'ari approach: affirm the attribute while negating any creaturely similarity.

Key Terms
سنية
سَنَاء
سَنَا
صفات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think 'suniyyah' literally means light, implying that God's attributes are physical light.
Correction: The commentator clarifies that 'suniyyah' is metaphorical: either meaning 'lofty' or comparing attributes to light in guiding, not that attributes are light, since light is a created accident.

Checkpoint
What are the two possible meanings of 'suniyyah' as explained in the commentary?
A) Beautiful and majestic
B) Lofty and luminous
C) Eternal and infinite
D) Powerful and merciful

Key Takeaway
The term 'suniyyah' for divine attributes can be understood as either 'lofty' or 'luminous' metaphorically, never as literal light.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The Two Meanings of 'Saniyya' in Divine Attributes
Lexical explanation of two meanings of 'saniyya'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two possible derivations of the term 'saniyya' when describing Allah's attributes and why they are metaphorical.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes are both lofty and illuminating, but not literally light.

In this passage, the commentator unpacks the word 'saniyya' used by the author. This term could be understood in two distinct ways, each drawing on a different Arabic root. Understanding this clarifies that when we describe Allah's attributes as 'light,' it is a powerful metaphor, not a physical description.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the English translation to get the gist.
Notice the two possibilities mentioned: 'like light' and 'lofty'.
2
Identify the two derivations
The commentary explains that 'saniyya' can derive from 'sanā'' (with madd) meaning loftiness, or from 'sanā' (with qasr) meaning light. Find each in the text.
The Qur'anic verse 24:43 is cited for the light meaning.
3
Understand the theological clarification
The commentator notes that calling attributes 'light' is a metaphor because light is an accident that cannot subsist in an attribute. Reflect on why this distinction matters.
This guards against literal anthropomorphism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم الإلهيات مطلقا (سَنِيَّه) أي: كالنُّور ، بجامع الاهتداء، أو معناه: رفيعة(۱)
(1) يريد له أن يقول : إِنَّ (سنية) في كلام المصنف فَعِيلَة ، ويجوز أن يكون مأخذها السَنَاء بالمد ـ وهو الرّفْعَة، فيكون المعنى: أن صفاته الرفيعة، أو يكون مأخذها السَنَا بالقصر ـ وهو الضوء والنور ، ومنه قوله سبحانه: ﴿يَكَادُ سَنَا بَرْقِهِ يَذْهَبُ بِالْأَبْصَرِ [النور: ٤٣] ويكون المعنى على تشبيه صفاته بالضوء، الا بمعنى أن صفاته قام بها النور؛ لأن النور عرض يستحيل قيامه بالصفة قديمة كانت أو حادثة ] محي الدين والشنواني.
The section on divine matters absolutely (saniyyah) i.e.: like light, due to the commonality of guidance, or its meaning: lofty. (1) He intends to say: Indeed (saniyyah) in the author's speech is fa‘īlah, and it is possible that its derivation is from as-sanā' (with elongation) which is loftiness, so the meaning is: His lofty attributes, or its derivation is from as-sanā (with shortening) which is light and illumination, and from it is His saying the Exalted: “The brightness of His lightning almost takes away the eyesight” [An-Nur: 43]; and the meaning is the likening of His attributes to light, except that His attributes are described by light because light is an accident impossible to subsist in an attribute, whether ancient or originated. Muhyī ad-Dīn and ash-Shanwānī.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is a lexical and theological explanation of the term 'saniyya' as used in the poem. The commentator first gives two possibilities: either it means 'like light' because it guides, or it means 'lofty'. The footnote then elaborates that 'saniyya' is a verbal noun form (fa‘īlah). It could derive from 'sanā'' (with madd) meaning loftiness, so the attributes are lofty. Or it could derive from 'sanā' (with qasr) meaning light, referencing Qur'an 24:43. The commentator clarifies that likening attributes to light is not literal because light is an accident that cannot subsist in an attribute. Thus the term metaphorically indicates guidance or elevation.

Defining the Attributes of Meanings
The author defines the seven attributes of meanings and states their nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of Sifat al-Ma'ani as existential attributes subsisting in the divine essence and necessitating specific judgments, and how they are distinguished from other attribute categories.

Core Idea
Sifat al-Ma'ani are real, existent attributes that make Allah what He is.

This passage introduces the third category of divine attributes: the attributes of meanings (Sifat al-Ma'ani). Unlike negative or relational attributes, these are positive, existential qualities that truly subsist in Allah's essence. The author begins with a Quranic proof to anchor the discussion, then provides a precise definition that distinguishes these attributes from mere concepts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own progression from Quranic proof to definition come through.
The Quranic verses serve as the decisive proof for affirming attributes without likeness.
2
Identify the key components of the definition
Find where the author states that Sifat al-Ma'ani are 'every attribute subsisting in a described entity, necessitating a judgment for it'. Note the two conditions: subsistence and necessitation.
3
Distinguish linguistic vs. technical meaning
The author explains that 'ma'na' linguistically includes all that corresponds to essence (even negative), but technically refers exclusively to subsisting existential attributes that yield a judgment. Contrast these two uses.
This clarifies why Sifat al-Ma'ani are a distinct category.
4
Apply the definition to the example of power
Reflect on the example given: power is an attribute subsisting in Allah's essence and necessitates that He is powerful. Ensure you see how the definition applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثالث: صفات المعاني السبعة
والأصل القاطع قوله تعالى: لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْبَصِيرُ [الشورى: 11]، قُلْ هُوَ اللهُ أَحَدٌ اللهُ الصَّمَدُ لَمْ يَلِدْ وَلَمْ يُولَدْ وَلَمْ يَكُن لَّهُ كُفُوًا أَحَدٌ [الإخلاص].
ثم شرع في بيان صفات المعاني ثالث أقسام الصفات، وهي عبارة عن كل صفة قائمة بموصوف موجبة له حكما.
ثم إن المعاني جمع معنى، والمعنى لغة ما قابل الذات فيشمل النفسية، والسلبية، وهو في اصطلاح علماء الكلام كل صفة قائمة بموصوف موجبة له حكما، ألا ترى أن القدرة صفة قائمة بذاته تعالى وأنها توجب له الكون قادرًا.
The third section: the seven attributes of meanings. And the decisive proof is His statement, the Exalted: 'There is nothing like unto Him, and He is the Hearing, the Seeing' [Al-Shura: 11], 'Say, He is Allah, [who is] One, Allah, the Eternal Refuge. He neither begets nor is born, nor is there to Him any equivalent' [Al-Ikhlas]. Then he began to explain the attributes of meanings, the third division of the attributes, and they are every attribute subsisting in a described entity, necessitating a judgment for it. Then indeed 'al-ma'ani' is the plural of 'ma'na', and 'ma'na' linguistically refers to what corresponds to the essence, thus including the existential and the negative attributes. In the terminology of the theologians, it is every attribute subsisting in a described entity, necessitating a judgment for it. Do you not see that power is an attribute subsisting in His Essence, the Exalted, and it necessitates that He is powerful.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage defines the third category of attributes, called 'Sifat al-Ma'ani' (attributes of meanings). The author begins by citing two Quranic verses as the decisive proof for affirming these attributes without similarity to creation: 'There is nothing like unto Him' negates anthropomorphism, while 'He is the Hearing, the Seeing' affirms the attributes. Then he states that the attributes of meanings are the third division of attributes (after existential and negative attributes). He defines them as: every attribute that subsists in a described entity (i.e., is existent in it) and necessitates a judgment for that entity. For example, the attribute of power subsists in the Essence of Allah and necessitates that He is described as 'powerful'. He then explains the term 'ma'ani' linguistically and terminologically. Linguistically, 'ma'na' is that which corresponds to the essence, encompassing both existential and negative attributes. In kalam terminology, it is specifically an existential attribute that subsists in a subject and produces a judgment. This definition distinguishes Sifat al-Ma'ani from merely relational or negative attributes.

Key Terms
صفات المعاني
صفة قائمة
موجبة لحكم
معنى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that Sifat al-Ma'ani are merely conceptual and not truly existent in the divine essence.
Correction: The definition emphasizes that they are 'qā'imah' (subsisting) and 'mūjibah' (necessitating), indicating real existence in Allah's essence.

Checkpoint

A) Attributes that are purely negative, like 'not being ignorant'.
B) Every attribute that subsists in a described entity and necessitates a judgment for it.
C) Attributes that are relational and depend on creation.
D) The essence of Allah Himself.

Key Takeaway
Sifat al-Ma'ani are real, existential attributes that subsist in Allah's essence and necessitate specific descriptions like power, knowledge, etc.

The Proof for Attributes of Meanings: Negation and Affirmation
Sanusi cites proof verses and explains their dual refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'anic verses cited prove the attributes of meanings by combining negation of similarity with affirmation of real attributes.

Core Idea
The verse balances tanzih and ithbat to establish attributes without resemblance.

Sanusi begins his explanation of the attributes of meanings by citing two decisive proof verses. These verses do double duty: they negate any likeness to Allah while affirming that He truly hears and sees. This lesson unpacks the theological logic behind the choice and order of these verses.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof verses
Read the Arabic passage containing Q. 42:11 and Q. 112. Then read the literal translation. Notice how the verses are presented as a single proof.
The two verses together establish both negation and affirmation.
2
Understand the dual function
The commentary explains that the first part of Q. 42:11 refutes the anthropomorphists (mujassimah) and the latter part refutes those who deny all attributes (mu'attilah). Identify these two functions.
3
Reflect on the order
Note why negation is placed before affirmation: detachment precedes adornment, and to prevent misunderstanding that hearing and seeing are like human faculties.
This ordering is deliberate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثالث: صِفَاتُ المَعاني السبعة
والأصل القاطع قوله تعالى: لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْبَصِيرُ [الشورى: 11]، ﴿قُلْ هُوَ اللهُ أَحَدٌ اللهُ الصَّمَدُ لَمْ يَلِدْ وَلَمْ يُولَدْ * وَلَمْ يَكُن لَّهُ كُفُوًا أَحَدٌ ﴾ [الإخلاص].
ثُمَّ شرع في بيان صفات المعاني ثالث أقسام الصفات، وهي عبارة عن كل صفة قائمة بموصوف موجبة له حكما.
هذه الآية صدرها تنزيه يردُّ على المجسمة، وعجزها إثبات يردُّ على المعطلة النافين للصفات الثبوتية. وقدَّم في الآية السَّلبَ على الإيجاب ؛ لأنَّ التخلية مقدمة على التحلية، ولكي لا يتوهم من السمع والبصر المشابهة للمألوف، وأن السمع بأذن وصماخ ، والبصر بحدقة.
إضافة «صفات» إلى «المعاني» في قولهم: صفات المعاني»، تحتمل أمرين، الأول: أن تكون هذه الإضافة بيانيَّةً ، ويكون المراد أنَّ هذه الصفات هي معانٍ وجودية، ونظيره قولنا: بلغ فلان مرتبة الاجتهاد» و«وصل فلان إلى درجة الإمامة»، فإنَّ المعنى: مرتبةُ الاجتهاد، ودرجة هي الإمامة، والثاني: أن تكون الإضافة على تقدير «من» أي: الصفات التي هي مِنَ المعاني، فإذا لاحظت أنّ علماء الكلام لم يصلوا إلى غير هذه السبع من بين المعاني، وأنه لا مزيد عليها عندهم تعين الوجه الأول ، وجواز الوجه الثاني مخصوص بما إذا نظرت إلى العبارة من حيث ذاتها، باعتبار أنَّ المعنى أعم ، يشمل كل موجود من صفات القديم والحادث.
ثمَّ إن المعاني جمع معنى، والمعنى لغة ما قابل الذات فيشمل النفسية، والسلبية، وهو في اصطلاح علماء الكلام (كل صفة قائمة بموصوف موجبة له حكما)، ألا تری أن القدرة صفة قائمة بذاته تعالى وأنها توجب له الكون قادرًا.
قوله: (كل صفة ) أي : وجودية، وإن كانت الصفة في اللغة تطلق على الوجودي وعلى العدمي كالقدم، وكون الصفة وجودية مفهوم من قوله : (قائمة) لأن العدمي لا يطلق عليه أنه قائم .
قوله: (موجبة له ) أي مستلزمة لا مؤثرة ، وقوله : (حكما) أي: وهو اللازم للصفة ، ككونه تعالى قادرا فإنه لازم للقدرة، فالحكم هو المعنوية، وفي الحقيقة المعاني والمعنوية متلازمان ؛ لكنهم لاحظوا الوجودي أصلا.
The third section: the seven attributes of meanings. And the decisive proof is His saying: 'Nothing is like Him, and He is the All-Hearing, the All-Seeing' [Q. 42:11], 'Say, He is Allah, the One, Allah the Eternal, He neither begets nor is begotten, nor is there to Him any equivalent' [Q. 112]. Then he began to explain the attributes of meanings, the third of the divisions of attributes, and it is every attribute subsisting in a described that necessitates for it a judgment. This verse: its first part is a negation that refutes the anthropomorphists, and its latter part is an affirmation that refutes the negators of affirmative attributes. And He presented in the verse negation before affirmation, because detachment precedes adornment, and so that no one might imagine from hearing and seeing a resemblance to the familiar, that hearing is with an ear and a canal, and seeing with a pupil. The addition of 'attributes' to 'meanings' in their saying 'attributes of meanings' admits two possibilities: first, that this addition is explanatory, meaning that these attributes are existential meanings; second, that the addition is estimated as 'min' (some of), i.e., the attributes that are from among meanings. Then the meanings is the plural of meaning, and meaning linguistically is what is opposed to the essence, thus including psychological and negative attributes, and in the terminology of the theologians it is 'every attribute subsisting in a described that necessitates for it a judgment'. His saying: 'every attribute' i.e., existential, even if the attribute in language applies to existential and to non-existential like eternity; His saying: 'necessitates for it' i.e., necessitates necessarily, not effectively; and His saying: 'a judgment' i.e., that which is necessary from the attribute.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage defines the third category of divine attributes—the attributes of meanings (sifat al-ma‘ani). It begins by citing two decisive proof verses: Q. 42:11 and Q. 112. The commentary explains that the first part of Q. 42:11 negates any likeness to Allah (refuting anthropomorphism) while the latter part affirms attributes of hearing and sight (refuting those who deny all attributes). Negation precedes affirmation to prevent any misconception that these attributes resemble human faculties. Then the passage gives the technical definition: attributes of meanings are 'every attribute subsisting in a described that necessitates for it a judgment'. It clarifies that the phrase 'attributes of meanings' can be interpreted either as an explanatory genitive (the attributes themselves are existential meanings) or as a partitive genitive (attributes that are part of meanings). The superiority of the first interpretation is argued from the fact that theologians limit the attributes of meanings to these seven. The definition is then unpacked: 'meaning' in theological terminology is an existential attribute that necessitates a judgment, e.g., power necessitates being powerful. The commentary further explains that the attribute must be existential (so it is 'subsisting') and that 'necessitates' means logical entailment, not causal influence.

Key Terms
تنزيه
إثبات
مجسمة
معطلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof verse only negates similarity to Allah without affirming real attributes.
Correction: The verse explicitly affirms 'He is the All-Hearing, the All-Seeing' after negating likeness, establishing real attributes without resemblance.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the verse present negation before affirmation?
A) Because negation is easier to understand.
B) Because detachment precedes adornment and to avoid imagining resemblance.
C) Because the verse was revealed in that order.
D) Because the affirmation was added later.

Key Takeaway
The proof for attributes of meanings uses both tanzih and ithbat to affirm real attributes without resemblance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read 'There is nothing like unto Him,' do you truly feel that Allah is beyond your imagination, or do you unconsciously picture Him in a certain way? What must you actively do to purify your belief in your heart?
?
The verse affirms that Allah hears and sees. Are you living as if you are always under His hearing and sight? What specific habits of yours would change if you truly believed this right now?
?
Negation (tanzih) came before affirmation (ithbat) to clear false ideas first. What false beliefs about Allah do you still hold in your heart that need to be removed so that you can truly affirm His attributes? Write down one and decide today to replace it with the truth from this lesson.

Defining Attributes of Meanings: The Technical Term Unpacked
Sanusi defines attributes of meanings and clarifies the phrase.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise definition of an attribute of meaning and the two interpretations of the phrase 'attributes of meanings'.

Core Idea
An attribute of meaning is an existential quality that logically necessitates a corresponding judgment.

After citing the proof, Sanusi gives the technical definition of attributes of meanings and clarifies the grammatical relationship between 'attributes' and 'meanings'. This lesson walks through the definition and the two possible interpretations.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition and its analysis
Read the passage from 'ثُمَّ شرع' to the end. Focus on the definition: 'كل صفة قائمة بموصوف موجبة له حكما'. Then read the literal translation.
This definition is the standard theological definition.
2
Understand the two interpretations
The author presents two ways to understand the phrase 'attributes of meanings': as an explanatory genitive (the attributes themselves are meanings) or as a partitive genitive (attributes that are part of meanings). Identify the reasoning for preferring the first.
3
Unpack the components of the definition
Examine each part: 'attribute' (existential), 'subsisting' (excludes non-existential), 'necessitates' (logical entailment, not causal effect), 'judgment' (the resulting description).

والأصل القاطع قوله تعالى: لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْبَصِيرُ [الشورى: 11]، ﴿قُلْ هُوَ اللهُ أَحَدٌ اللهُ الصَّمَدُ لَمْ يَلِدْ وَلَمْ يُولَدْ * وَلَمْ يَكُن لَّهُ كُفُوًا أَحَدٌ ﴾ [الإخلاص].
ثُمَّ شرع في بيان صفات المعاني ثالث أقسام الصفات، وهي عبارة عن كل صفة قائمة بموصوف موجبة له حكما.
هذه الآية صدرها تنزيه يردُّ على المجسمة، وعجزها إثبات يردُّ على المعطلة النافين للصفات الثبوتية. وقدَّم في الآية السَّلبَ على الإيجاب ؛ لأنَّ التخلية مقدمة على التحلية، ولكي لا يتوهم من السمع والبصر المشابهة للمألوف، وأن السمع بأذن وصماخ ، والبصر بحدقة.
إضافة «صفات» إلى «المعاني» في قولهم: صفات المعاني»، تحتمل أمرين، الأول: أن تكون هذه الإضافة بيانيَّةً ، ويكون المراد أنَّ هذه الصفات هي معانٍ وجودية، ونظيره قولنا: بلغ فلان مرتبة الاجتهاد» و«وصل فلان إلى درجة الإمامة»، فإنَّ المعنى: مرتبةُ الاجتهاد، ودرجة هي الإمامة، والثاني: أن تكون الإضافة على تقدير «من» أي: الصفات التي هي مِنَ المعاني، فإذا لاحظت أنّ علماء الكلام لم يصلوا إلى غير هذه السبع من بين المعاني، وأنه لا مزيد عليها عندهم تعين الوجه الأول ، وجواز الوجه الثاني مخصوص بما إذا نظرت إلى العبارة من حيث ذاتها، باعتبار أنَّ المعنى أعم ، يشمل كل موجود من صفات القديم والحادث.

قوله: (كل صفة ) أي : وجودية، وإن كانت الصفة في اللغة تطلق على الوجودي وعلى العدمي كالقدم، وكون الصفة وجودية مفهوم من قوله : (قائمة) لأن العدمي لا يطلق عليه أنه قائم .
قوله: (موجبة له ) أي مستلزمة لا مؤثرة ، وقوله : (حكما) أي: وهو اللازم للصفة ، ككونه تعالى قادرا فإنه لازم للقدرة، فالحكم هو المعنوية، وفي الحقيقة المعاني والمعنوية متلازمان ؛ لكنهم لاحظوا الوجودي أصلا.

The Attribute of Power: Definition and Proof
Defines qudra and proves its necessity from creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the conventional definition of divine power (qudra) and the rational argument demonstrating its necessity in God.

Core Idea
God's power is the eternal ability to create and destroy, proven from creation itself.

Sanusi introduces the first of the seven essential attributes: power (qudra). He gives a precise conventional definition and immediately clarifies that it is only a description (rasm), not a real definition of God's essence. Then he provides a brief but powerful proof: since there are temporal things, they must come from an eternal maker acting through power and choice, not by blind compulsion. This lesson unpacks both the definition and the proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition carefully
The definition of power mentions 'eternal attribute', 'bringing into existence and destruction', and 'in accordance with will'. Note each component.
The definition is conventional, not essential.
2
Understand the proof
The proof moves from the existence of temporal things to an eternal maker who acts through power and choice. Identify the three premises.
The proof refutes the idea of compulsion (ījāb).
3
Note the rasm warning
Sanusi emphasizes that this definition is a 'rasm', a descriptive outline, not a real definition. Understand why that matters.
We cannot define God's essence, only describe attributes.
4
Reflect on the metaphor caution
The phrase 'through which is achieved' should not imply toil. The effect is truly from God's essence, and saying 'power is effective' is metaphorical.
This safeguards against anthropomorphism.
5
Review the key terms
Familiarize yourself with the Arabic terms: قدرة, إيجاد وإعدام, على وفق الإرادة, etc. They are central to the discourse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم الإلهيات
وهي سبع
[ ١ - صفة القدرة، تعريفها، وأدلة ثبوتها ]
۲۷ - وَقُدْرَةٌ إرَادَةٌ وَغَايَرَتْ أَمْرًا وَعْلِمًا والرِّضَا كما ثَبَتْ
فالأُولَى ما أشار إليها بقوله (وَ) واجب له تعالى (قُدْرَةٌ) كاملة ، وهي عُرفًا: صفة أزليَّة يتأتى بها إيجاد كلّ ممكن وإعدامه على وَفْقِ الإرادة، وإنَّما وجبت له تعالى ؛ لأنَّه صانع قديمٌ له مصنوع حادث ، وصدور الحادثِ عن القديم إنَّما يُتصوّر بطريق القُدرة والاختيار ، دونَ الإيجاب
انحصار صفات المعاني في السبع هو بالنظر إلى ما قام الدليل عليه تفصيلا ، مع قطع النَّظر عن صفات وقع فيها خلاف ولم يقم الدليل على أنها صفات زائدة على هذه السبع، كالإدراك والتكوين ، وسيأتي للمصنف والشارح التّعرض لصفة الإدراك ، وسنتكلم عن ذلك هناك
قوله: (يتأتى) ليس ظاهره في المعاناة والاستعانة مرادا ؛ لاستحالة ذلك عليه سبحانه، نعم التأثير حقيقةً للذات وقولهم: القدرة فعالة .. مجاز لا كفر ما لم يرد الانفكاك والاستقلال.
الكلام في صفة القدرة يتعلق بها من ثلاثة وجوه الوجه الأول: في بيان معناها ، والوجه الثاني : في بيان الدليل على وجوبها له سبحانه، والوجه الثالث في بيان ما تتعلق به القدرة . أما الكلام على معناها: فالقدرة في اللغة: القوَّة والاستطاعة وضد العجز، وفي اصطلاح علماء الكلام ما ذكره الشارح بقوله : وهي عرفًا صفة أزلية قائمة بذاته يتأتى بها إيجاد كل ممكن وإعدامه على وفق الإرادة»، وقبل أن نشرح لك هذا التعريف تنبهك إلى أنَّ هذا التعريف رسم وليس حدا حقيقيا ؛ لأن الحد الحقيقي لا يكون إلا بذكر ذاتيات المحدود، ونحن لا نعلم كنه ذاته سبحانه ولا كنه صفة من صفاته ، وإنما نعلم خصائص هذه الذات وأوصافها ، وخصائص الصفات ، وهذا الكلام يجري في كل التعاريف المذكورة للصفات . =
The section on divine matters. And they are seven. [1 - The attribute of power, its definition, and proofs of its establishment.] 27 - And power, will, difference, command, knowledge, and pleasure as established. The first is what he alluded to by his saying: 'And obligatory for Him, exalted, is perfect power.' And it is conventionally: an eternal attribute through which is achieved the bringing into existence of every possible and its destruction in accordance with the will. And it is obligatory for Him, exalted, because He is an eternal Maker who has a temporal made thing, and the occurrence of the temporal from the eternal is only conceivable by way of power and choice, not by compulsion. The restriction of attributes of meanings to seven is with regard to what the evidence has established in detail, disregarding attributes concerning which there was disagreement and for which evidence did not establish that they are additional to these seven, such as perception and generation. His saying: 'through which is achieved' – its apparent meaning of toil and seeking help is not intended, due to the impossibility of that for Him. Yes, the effect is truly through the essence, and their saying 'power is effective' is a metaphor, not disbelief, as long as separation and independence are not intended. The discussion of the attribute of power relates to it from three aspects: the first aspect is to explain its meaning; the second is to explain the proof of its obligatoriness for Him; the third is to explain what power applies to. As for the discussion of its meaning: power in language means strength and ability, the opposite of inability, and in the terminology of the theologians it is what the commentator mentioned: 'It is conventionally: an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence through which is achieved the bringing into existence of every possible and its destruction in accordance with the will.' And before we explain to you this definition, we alert you that this definition is a description (rasm) and not a real definition, because a real definition can only be by mentioning the essentials of the defined, and we do not know the reality of His essence nor the reality of any of His attributes; rather we know the characteristics of this essence and its descriptions, and the characteristics of the attributes, and this statement applies to all the definitions mentioned for the attributes.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage introduces the first of the seven attributes of meanings: power (qudra). It begins with a line of poetry listing the seven: power, will, difference, command, knowledge, pleasure. The commentary then defines power conventionally as 'an eternal attribute through which is achieved the bringing into existence of every possible and its destruction in accordance with the will.' The proof for its necessity is that Allah is an eternal creator of temporal things; the only way a temporal thing can proceed from an eternal agent is through power and choice, not by compulsion (jabr). The passage then clarifies that the enumeration of these seven attributes is based on detailed evidence, excluding disputed attributes like perception (idrak) and generation (takwin). It also warns that the word 'through which is achieved' does not imply toil or seeking help, which are impossible for Allah; the effect is truly from the essence. Finally, it states that the definition given is a 'rasm' (descriptive definition) not a 'hadd haqiqi' (real definition), because we cannot know the unknowable essence and attributes of Allah. This note applies to all definitions of attributes.

إيجاد وإعدام
على وفق الإرادة
صانع قديم
مصنوع حادث
الاختيار
الإيجاب
رسم
حد حقيقي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that God's creation of the universe is necessary or automatic, like a cause producing an effect by compulsion.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the temporal proceeds from the eternal only through power and choice (qudra wa ikhtiyār), not by compulsion (ījāb).

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is power (qudra) necessarily attributed to Allah?
A) Because the Qur'an explicitly mentions it.
B) Because He is an eternal maker of temporal things, which can only proceed through power and choice.
C) Because power is the only attribute that can be proven rationally.
D) Because power is the same as will.

Key Takeaway
Power (qudra) is defined as an eternal attribute enabling creation and destruction by will, and its necessity is proven by the existence of temporal things requiring an eternal agent of choice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You recite that God's power is eternal and sufficient for everything, but when you face a crushing difficulty, do you first turn to your own ability or to His? What would it actually look like for you to genuinely entrust that one specific burden to His qudra today?
?
If God's power is the only true cause of every event, what does that mean for the way you view your own efforts and achievements? Are you secretly proud of your successes as if you accomplished them alone? How can you actively attribute each good result back to His power from now on?
?
The passage warns that we cannot know the reality of God's attributes, only their characteristics. Are you content with that limitation, or does your heart crave a detailed understanding that leads to pride? What can you do today to humble yourself before the mystery of His qudra rather than demand explanations?
