The Definition of Divine Power and Its Necessity
Definition of qudra and proof of its necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of divine power (qudra) and the rational argument for why it is necessary for Allah.

Core Idea
Divine power is the eternal attribute that creates and destroys all possibilities according to will.

The author begins by quoting the matn of al-Jawharah and then provides the conventional definition of qudra. He also gives the theological rationale: only power and choice can explain how an eternal God produces temporal creation. This lesson unpacks that foundational definition.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse. Then read the translation to get the overall meaning.
Notice the compressed style of the poem line.
2
Identify the definition components
The definition has several parts: 'eternal attribute', 'through which is possible', 'bringing into existence of every possible', 'annihilation', 'in accordance with will'. Note each one.
3
Understand the necessity argument
Ask yourself why qudra is obligatory for Allah. The passage argues from the fact of temporal creation. Reflect on why power and choice are needed rather than natural necessity.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقُدْرَةٌ إرَادَةٌ وَغَايَرَتْ أَمْرًا وَعْلِمًا والرِّضَا كما ثَبَتْ
فالأُولَى ما أشار إليها بقوله (وَ) واجب له تعالى (قُدْرَةٌ) كاملة ، وهي عرفًا: صفة أزليَّة يتأتى بها إيجاد كلّ ممكن وإعدامه على وَفْقِ الإرادة، وإنَّما وجبت له تعالى ؛ لأنَّه صانع قديمٌ له مصنوع حادث ، وصدور الحادثِ عن القديم إنَّما يُتصوّر بطريق القُدرة والاختيار ، دونَ الإيجاب
وبعد ؛ فاعلم أن قولنا: (صفة) ، كالجنس في التعريف ، وقولنا : يتأتى بها إيجاد كل ممكن وإعدامه» ، إشارة إلى تعلُّق من تعلقات القدرة يسمى: «التعلق الصَّلوحي القديم» أو «التَّعلق الصَّلَاحي القديم ، وسيأتي بيانه مع سائر تعلقات القدرة قريبا، وقولنا: «بها»، إشارة إلى أنَّ التأثير حقيقة للذات ، وإسنادُ التأثير إلى القدرة مجاز، لكون القدرة سببا في التأثير، وقولنا: «كل ممكن»، قيد للاحتراز ، يخرج به الواجب والمستحيل، فإنهما مما لا تعلق للقدرة به ، وذلك لأنها لو تعلقت بالواجب لم يصح أن تعدمه ؛ لأن الواجب لا يقبل العدم، ولا يصح أن توجده ؛ لأن في إيجادها إياه تحصيل الحاصل ، ولو تعلقت بالمستحيل لم يصح أن توجده ؛ لأن المستحيل لا يقبل الوجود ، ولا يصح أن تعدمه ؛ لأنَّ في إعدامها إياه تحصيل الحاصل ، ومعنى قولنا: على وفق الإرادة» أن كل ما خصصه الله تعالى بإرادته أبرزه بقدرته ، فتعلق الإرادة لكونه أزليّاً سابق على تعلق القدرة لكونه تنجيزاً حادثًا ، ومن هذه العبارة تدرك أن الترتيب حاصل بين تعلق صفتي القدرة والإرادة ، وأنه لا ترتيب بين نفس الصفتين ؛ لا ترتيب فيه ، وإلا يكن الأمر كذلك كان المتأخّر منهما حادثا ، ومن العلماء من عرف القدرة بقوله : «صفة تؤثر في إيجاد الممكن وإعدامه ، فقوله : (صفة) ، كالجنس في التعريف يشمل جميع الصفات، وقوله: (تؤثر»، كالفصل الأوَّلِ يَخْرجُ به جميع ما لا تأثير له من الصفات، كالعلم والحياة والسمع والبصر والكلام ،ونحوها ما عدا الإرادة، وقولنا: «في إيجاد الممكن ـ إلخ» ، كفصل ثانٍ تَخْرُجُ به الإرادة، فإنَّها لا تؤثر في الإيجادِ والإعدام، وإنما تؤثر في تخصيص الممكن ببعض ما يجوز عليه كما يأتي بيانه قريبا، وهذا بناء على أنَّ التَّخصيص المذكور نوعٌ مِن التأثير ، وهو الصحيح، فإن ذهبت إلى أنَّ التَّخصيص ليس تأثيرا ، كانت الإرادة خارجة بالفصل الأوَّلِ ، وكان قوله : «في إيجاد الممكن وإعدامه» لبيان تعلق القدرة.
And power, will, and they differed from command and knowledge and satisfaction as established. The first is what he pointed to by his saying: 'And obligatory for Him, exalted, is perfect power'. And it is conventionally: an eternal attribute through which is possible the bringing into existence of every possible thing and its annihilation in accordance with will. And it is obligatory for Him, exalted, because He is an eternal maker having a temporal made thing, and the emanation of the temporal from the eternal is only conceivable by way of power and choice, not by necessity. After that, know that our saying 'attribute' is like the genus in the definition, and our saying 'through which is possible the bringing into existence of every possible thing and its annihilation' is an indication to a relation (ta'alluq) from among the relations of power called 'the ancient suitability relation' or 'the ancient fitness relation', and its explanation will come soon along with the rest of the relations of power. And our saying 'by it' is an indication that the effect (ta'thir) is in reality for the essence, and the attribution of effect to power is metaphorical, because power is a cause of the effect. And our saying 'every possible' is a restrictive condition to exclude, by it, the necessary and the impossible: they are such that power has no relation to them. That is because if it were related to the necessary, it would not be valid to annihilate it because the necessary does not admit non-existence, nor would it be valid to bring it into existence because bringing it into existence would be the acquisition of what is already obtained. And if it were related to the impossible, it would not be valid to bring it into existence because the impossible does not admit existence, nor would it be valid to annihilate it because annihilating it would be the acquisition of what is already obtained. And the meaning of our saying 'in accordance with will' is that everything that Allah, exalted, has specified by His will He manifests by His power. So the relation of will, being eternal, precedes the relation of power, being a temporal actualization (tanjiz). And from this statement you understand that there is order between the relations of the two attributes of power and will, and that there is no order between the two attributes themselves; there is no order in them, for if it were otherwise, the later of them would be temporal. And some scholars have defined power by their saying: 'An attribute that effects the bringing into existence of the possible and its annihilation'. So his saying 'attribute' is like the genus in the definition, encompassing all attributes. His saying 'effects' is like the first differentia, by which are excluded all attributes that have no effect, such as knowledge, life, hearing, sight, speech, and the like, except will. And our saying 'in bringing into existence the possible, etc.' is like a second differentia, by which will is excluded, because it does not effect bringing into existence and annihilation; rather, it effects the specification (takhsis) of the possible to some of what is permissible for it, as will come soon. And this is based on the view that the mentioned specification is a type of effect, and that is correct. If you hold that specification is not an effect, then will would be excluded by the first differentia, and his saying 'in bringing into existence the possible and its annihilation' would be for clarifying the relation of power.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage provides the definition of the divine attribute of power (qudra) and explains its components. The author begins by quoting the verse from al-Jawharah: 'And power, will, and they differ from command and knowledge and satisfaction as established.' He then states that the first attribute referred to is power, which is wajib (obligatory) for Allah. The conventional definition is given: 'an eternal attribute through which is possible the bringing into existence of every possible thing and its annihilation in accordance with will.' The necessity of power for Allah is argued on the basis that He is an eternal maker with temporal creation—only power and choice (not necessity) can explain the production of the temporal from the eternal.

The author then systematically explains each term of the definition:
1. 'Attribute' (sifa) functions as the genus, encompassing all attributes.
2. 'Through which is possible...' refers to the 'suitability relation' (al-ta'alluq al-saluhi) of power, which is ancient (qadim). The effect (ta'thir) is truly from the essence, not the attribute; attributing effect to power is metaphorical, as power is only a cause.
3. 'Every possible' excludes the necessary (wajib) and the impossible (mustahil). Both are not subject to power: the necessary cannot be annihilated or brought into existence anew, and the impossible cannot be brought into existence or annihilated (since it is already non-existent).
4. 'In accordance with will' indicates that whatever Allah wills, He brings into being by His power. The relation of will is eternal and precedes the relation of power, which is temporal (tanjiz). There is order between these relations but not between the attributes themselves; otherwise the later attribute would be temporal.

The author then presents an alternative definition: 'an attribute that effects the bringing into existence of the possible and its annihilation.' He analyzes this definition as having two differentiae: 'effects' excludes all non-effective attributes (knowledge, life, etc., except will), and 'in bringing into existence the possible' excludes will, since will does not effect existence but rather specification. This shows that the relation of power is to the act of creation and annihilation, while will is related to specification. The passage concludes by noting that if specification is not considered a type of effect, then will is already excluded by the first differentia.

Throughout, the author emphasizes that the definition is a resm (descriptive definition) not a hadd haqiqi (true definition) because we do not know the essence of God's attributes—a point from a footnote that is not in the main text but relevant. The passage clarifies the scope and nuances of the attribute of power.

Key Terms
القدرة
الصفة الأزلية
الإيجاد والإعدام
الممكن
الإرادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think divine power is the same as divine will or that power is not a distinct attribute.
Correction: The passage defines power as a distinct attribute (sifa) through which creation occurs, and distinguishes it from will by noting the relation of power is temporal actualization while will is eternal.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is power (qudra) necessary for Allah?
A) Because He is eternal.
B) Because He has temporal creation and the production requires power and choice.
C) Because He is all-knowing.
D) Because He is all-powerful.

Key Takeaway
Divine power is the eternal attribute by which Allah creates and destroys all possibilities in accordance with His will, and it is necessary because only power and choice can explain the emanation of temporal from eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that Allah's power is eternal and creates all possibilities according to His will, what plans have you made this week that assume your own power is sufficient? Write down one specific decision you need to consciously surrender to His will today.
?
If everything temporal—including your next breath—requires Allah's power and choice (not blind necessity), how does that change your reaction to the last trial you faced? Commit to verbalizing 'Alhamdulillah' before reacting the next time something goes wrong.
?
The passage teaches that Allah's power is not by necessity but by will and choice. Do you live as though events are merely mechanical causes, or do you see His personal hand in them? List one area where you can actively trust His choice over your own preference today.

Explaining the Terms of the Definition of Power
Explanation of the components of the definition of qudra

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the function of each term in the definition of divine power and why it excludes the necessary and impossible.

Core Idea
Each word in the definition of power is a technical restriction that clarifies its scope.

The author now systematically explains each part of the definition: 'attribute' as genus, 'through which' as the suitability relation, 'by it' to clarify true agency, and 'every possible' to exclude the necessary and impossible. This logical unpacking trains the student in precise theological reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the explanation of 'attribute'
Notice that 'attribute' (sifa) functions as the genus in the definition, including all attributes of Allah. This is the first term explained.
The definition is a resm (descriptive definition), not a hadd haqiqi.
2
Understand 'through which is possible'
This refers to the 'suitability relation' (al-ta'alluq al-saluhi), which is ancient. The effect (ta'thir) is actually from the essence, not the attribute.
The attribution of effect to power is metaphorical.
3
Grasp the exclusion of necessary and impossible
The term 'every possible' is a restrictive condition to exclude the necessary (wajib) and impossible (mustahil). Read the reasoning for each.
Power cannot bring into existence what already exists necessarily, nor annihilate what is impossible.

What is the function of the phrase 'every possible' in the definition of power?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

The Scope of Power: Exclusion of Necessary and Impossible, and Relation to Will
Detailed scope of power and its relation to will

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why power cannot relate to the necessary or impossible, and how power and will are ordered in their relations.

Core Idea
Power only governs the possible; necessary and impossible are outside its scope, and will precedes power in order.

After defining power, the author delves deeper into its scope: power cannot affect the necessary (which cannot cease) or the impossible (which cannot become). He then explains the relationship between power and will: will's relation is eternal, power's relation is temporal. Finally, he presents an alternative definition that separates power from will by two differentiae.

Guided Path
1
Read the justification for excluding necessary and impossible
The author gives detailed reasoning: if power related to the necessary, it could not annihilate it (since it cannot not exist) nor create it anew (since it already exists). Similarly for the impossible.
This shows the logical boundaries of divine power.
2
Understand the ordering of will and power
The relation of will (ta'alluq al-irada) is eternal and precedes the relation of power (ta'alluq al-qudra), which is temporal. There is no order between the attributes themselves.
This preserves the eternity of both attributes.
3
Analyze the alternative definition
Some define power as 'an attribute that effects the bringing into existence of the possible and its annihilation.' This definition uses two differentiae: 'effects' excludes non-effective attributes, and 'in bringing into existence' excludes will (which only specifies, not creates).
The alternative definition is based on the view that specification is a type of effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقُدْرَةٌ إرَادَةٌ وَغَايَرَتْ أَمْرًا وَعْلِمًا والرِّضَا كما ثَبَتْ
فالأُولَى ما أشار إليها بقوله (وَ) واجب له تعالى (قُدْرَةٌ) كاملة ، وهي عرفًا: صفة أزليَّة يتأتى بها إيجاد كلّ ممكن وإعدامه على وَفْقِ الإرادة، وإنَّما وجبت له تعالى ؛ لأنَّه صانع قديمٌ له مصنوع حادث ، وصدور الحادثِ عن القديم إنَّما يُتصوّر بطريق القُدرة والاختيار ، دونَ الإيجاب
وبعد ؛ فاعلم أن قولنا: (صفة) ، كالجنس في التعريف ، وقولنا : يتأتى بها إيجاد كل ممكن وإعدامه» ، إشارة إلى تعلُّق من تعلقات القدرة يسمى: «التعلق الصَّلوحي القديم» أو «التَّعلق الصَّلَاحي القديم ، وسيأتي بيانه مع سائر تعلقات القدرة قريبا، وقولنا: «بها»، إشارة إلى أنَّ التأثير حقيقة للذات ، وإسنادُ التأثير إلى القدرة مجاز، لكون القدرة سببا في التأثير، وقولنا: «كل ممكن»، قيد للاحتراز ، يخرج به الواجب والمستحيل، فإنهما مما لا تعلق للقدرة به ، وذلك لأنها لو تعلقت بالواجب لم يصح أن تعدمه ؛ لأن الواجب لا يقبل العدم، ولا يصح أن توجده ؛ لأن في إيجادها إياه تحصيل الحاصل ، ولو تعلقت بالمستحيل لم يصح أن توجده ؛ لأن المستحيل لا يقبل الوجود ، ولا يصح أن تعدمه ؛ لأنَّ في إعدامها إياه تحصيل الحاصل ، ومعنى قولنا: على وفق الإرادة» أن كل ما خصصه الله تعالى بإرادته أبرزه بقدرته ، فتعلق الإرادة لكونه أزليّاً سابق على تعلق القدرة لكونه تنجيزاً حادثًا ، ومن هذه العبارة تدرك أن الترتيب حاصل بين تعلق صفتي القدرة والإرادة ، وأنه لا ترتيب بين نفس الصفتين ؛ لا ترتيب فيه ، وإلا يكن الأمر كذلك كان المتأخّر منهما حادثا ، ومن العلماء من عرف القدرة بقوله : «صفة تؤثر في إيجاد الممكن وإعدامه ، فقوله : (صفة) ، كالجنس في التعريف يشمل جميع الصفات، وقوله: (تؤثر»، كالفصل الأوَّلِ يَخْرجُ به جميع ما لا تأثير له من الصفات، كالعلم والحياة والسمع والبصر والكلام ،ونحوها ما عدا الإرادة، وقولنا: «في إيجاد الممكن ـ إلخ» ، كفصل ثانٍ تَخْرُجُ به الإرادة، فإنَّها لا تؤثر في الإيجادِ والإعدام، وإنما تؤثر في تخصيص الممكن ببعض ما يجوز عليه كما يأتي بيانه قريبا، وهذا بناء على أنَّ التَّخصيص المذكور نوعٌ مِن التأثير ، وهو الصحيح، فإن ذهبت إلى أنَّ التَّخصيص ليس تأثيرا ، كانت الإرادة خارجة بالفصل الأوَّلِ ، وكان قوله : «في إيجاد الممكن وإعدامه» لبيان تعلق القدرة.
And power, will, and they differed from command and knowledge and satisfaction as established. The first is what he pointed to by his saying: 'And obligatory for Him, exalted, is perfect power'. And it is conventionally: an eternal attribute through which is possible the bringing into existence of every possible thing and its annihilation in accordance with will. And it is obligatory for Him, exalted, because He is an eternal maker having a temporal made thing, and the emanation of the temporal from the eternal is only conceivable by way of power and choice, not by necessity. After that, know that our saying 'attribute' is like the genus in the definition, and our saying 'through which is possible the bringing into existence of every possible thing and its annihilation' is an indication to a relation (ta'alluq) from among the relations of power called 'the ancient suitability relation' or 'the ancient fitness relation', and its explanation will come soon along with the rest of the relations of power. And our saying 'by it' is an indication that the effect (ta'thir) is in reality for the essence, and the attribution of effect to power is metaphorical, because power is a cause of the effect. And our saying 'every possible' is a restrictive condition to exclude, by it, the necessary and the impossible: they are such that power has no relation to them. That is because if it were related to the necessary, it would not be valid to annihilate it because the necessary does not admit non-existence, nor would it be valid to bring it into existence because bringing it into existence would be the acquisition of what is already obtained. And if it were related to the impossible, it would not be valid to bring it into existence because the impossible does not admit existence, nor would it be valid to annihilate it because annihilating it would be the acquisition of what is already obtained. And the meaning of our saying 'in accordance with will' is that everything that Allah, exalted, has specified by His will He manifests by His power. So the relation of will, being eternal, precedes the relation of power, being a temporal actualization (tanjiz). And from this statement you understand that there is order between the relations of the two attributes of power and will, and that there is no order between the two attributes themselves; there is no order in them, for if it were otherwise, the later of them would be temporal. And some scholars have defined power by their saying: 'An attribute that effects the bringing into existence of the possible and its annihilation'. So his saying 'attribute' is like the genus in the definition, encompassing all attributes. His saying 'effects' is like the first differentia, by which are excluded all attributes that have no effect, such as knowledge, life, hearing, sight, speech, and the like, except will. And our saying 'in bringing into existence the possible, etc.' is like a second differentia, by which will is excluded, because it does not effect bringing into existence and annihilation; rather, it effects the specification (takhsis) of the possible to some of what is permissible for it, as will come soon. And this is based on the view that the mentioned specification is a type of effect, and that is correct. If you hold that specification is not an effect, then will would be excluded by the first differentia, and his saying 'in bringing into existence the possible and its annihilation' would be for clarifying the relation of power.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage provides the definition of the divine attribute of power (qudra) and explains its components. The author begins by quoting the verse from al-Jawharah: 'And power, will, and they differ from command and knowledge and satisfaction as established.' He then states that the first attribute referred to is power, which is wajib (obligatory) for Allah. The conventional definition is given: 'an eternal attribute through which is possible the bringing into existence of every possible thing and its annihilation in accordance with will.' The necessity of power for Allah is argued on the basis that He is an eternal maker with temporal creation—only power and choice (not necessity) can explain the production of the temporal from the eternal.

The author then systematically explains each term of the definition:
1. 'Attribute' (sifa) functions as the genus, encompassing all attributes.
2. 'Through which is possible...' refers to the 'suitability relation' (al-ta'alluq al-saluhi) of power, which is ancient (qadim). The effect (ta'thir) is truly from the essence, not the attribute; attributing effect to power is metaphorical, as power is only a cause.
3. 'Every possible' excludes the necessary (wajib) and the impossible (mustahil). Both are not subject to power: the necessary cannot be annihilated or brought into existence anew, and the impossible cannot be brought into existence or annihilated (since it is already non-existent).
4. 'In accordance with will' indicates that whatever Allah wills, He brings into being by His power. The relation of will is eternal and precedes the relation of power, which is temporal (tanjiz). There is order between these relations but not between the attributes themselves; otherwise the later attribute would be temporal.

The author then presents an alternative definition: 'an attribute that effects the bringing into existence of the possible and its annihilation.' He analyzes this definition as having two differentiae: 'effects' excludes all non-effective attributes (knowledge, life, etc., except will), and 'in bringing into existence the possible' excludes will, since will does not effect existence but rather specification. This shows that the relation of power is to the act of creation and annihilation, while will is related to specification. The passage concludes by noting that if specification is not considered a type of effect, then will is already excluded by the first differentia.

Throughout, the author emphasizes that the definition is a resm (descriptive definition) not a hadd haqiqi (true definition) because we do not know the essence of God's attributes—a point from a footnote that is not in the main text but relevant. The passage clarifies the scope and nuances of the attribute of power.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that power can affect the necessary or impossible, or that will and power are identical.
Correction: The passage clearly states power does not relate to necessary/impossible, and distinguishes will and power by their effects: will specifies, power creates.

Checkpoint
Why can power not annihilate the impossible?
A) Because the impossible is too strong for power.
B) Because annihilating the impossible would be acquiring what is already obtained (it already does not exist).
C) Because power only creates, it does not annihilate.
D) Because the impossible is not subject to power at all, but annihilation is not the issue.

Key Takeaway
Power relates only to possible entities; necessary and impossible are outside its scope. Will precedes power in order, and an alternative definition uses two differentiae to separate power from other attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make du'a, do you sometimes ask for things that are logically impossible (e.g., to change the past) and then feel your prayer is unanswered? How does knowing that Allah's power only relates to the possible change the way you approach supplication? Will you commit to aligning your requests with what is possible, trusting that His will and power work together for your good?
?
The passage teaches that Allah's power cannot annihilate the necessary—Himself and His attributes. Does this truth reassure you that Allah's nature is unchanging and reliable? Where in your life have you doubted His consistency, and how will you now build your trust in His permanence?
?
Will precedes power in order: nothing happens without being first willed by Allah. Have you ever acted as if events can occur outside His will, perhaps through worry or resentment about your circumstances? What would change in your heart if you fully accepted that every possible event is first specified by His will before being executed by His power? Can you surrender one area of your life today to this truth?

Divine Attributes

The Definition of Divine Power and Its Parts
The author defines divine power and explains each term of the definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the divine attribute of power (qudra) and how each part of the definition excludes other possibilities.

Core Idea
Power attaches only to possible things, not to the necessary or impossible.

This lesson unpacks the standard definition of divine power. The author carefully explains each phrase, showing how it functions as a genus or differentia, and what it excludes. Understanding this definition is essential for grasping how God's power relates to creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition passage
Read the Arabic passage that defines power. Pay attention to the phrases: 'attribute', 'by which comes about...', 'every possible thing', 'in accordance with will'.
The definition is broken down word by word.
2
Analyze the role of each phrase
The author explains that 'attribute' is the genus, 'by it' shows the true effect is from the essence, 'every possible thing' excludes necessary and impossible, and 'in accordance with will' links power to will.
Notice how each part narrows the definition.
3
Understand the exclusion of necessary and impossible
Reflect on why power cannot attach to the necessary (cannot be annihilated, existence is redundant) and the impossible (cannot be brought into existence, non-existence is redundant).
This is a key insight in kalam.
4
Grasp the relation between will and power
The text explains that will's attachment is eternal and precedes power's temporal attachment. There is order between attachments, not between the attributes themselves.
This preserves divine simplicity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد ؛ فاعلم أن قولنا: (صفة) ، كالجنس في التعريف ، وقولنا : يتأتى بها إيجاد كل ممكن وإعدامه» ، إشارة إلى تعلُّق من تعلقات القدرة يسمى: «التعلق الصَّلوحي القديم» أو «التَّعلق الصَّلَاحي القديم ، وسيأتي بيانه مع سائر تعلقات القدرة قريبا، وقولنا: «بها»، إشارة إلى أنَّ التأثير حقيقة للذات ، وإسنادُ التأثير إلى القدرة مجاز، لكون القدرة سببا في التأثير، وقولنا: «كل ممكن»، قيد للاحتراز ، يخرج به الواجب والمستحيل، فإنهما مما لا تعلق للقدرة به ، وذلك لأنها لو تعلقت بالواجب لم يصح أن تعدمه ؛ لأن الواجب لا يقبل العدم، يصح توجده ؛ لأن في إيجادها إياه تحصيل الحاصل ، ولو تعلقت بالمستحيل لم يصح أن توجده ؛ لأن المستحيل لا يقبل الوجود ، ولا يصح أن تعدمه ؛ لأنَّ في إعدامها إياه تحصيل الحاصل ، ومعنى قولنا: على وفق الإرادة» أن كل ما خصصه الله تعالى بإرادته أبرزه بقدرته ، فتعلق الإرادة لكونه أزليّاً سابق على تعلق القدرة لكونه تنجيزاً حادثًا ، ومن هذه العبارة تدرك [؟] أن الترتيب حاصل بين تعلق صفتي القدرة والإرادة ، وأنه لا ترتيب بين نفس الصفتين ؛ لا ترتيب فيه ، وإلا يكن الأمر كذلك كان المتأخّر منهما حادثا ، ومن العلماء من عرف القديم القدرة بقوله : «صفة تؤثر في إيجاد الممكن وإعدامه ، فقوله : (صفة) ، كالجنس في التعريف يشمل جميع الصفات، وقوله: (تؤثر»، كالفصل الأوَّلِ يَخْرجُ به جميع ما لا تأثير له من الصفات، كالعلم والحياة والسمع والبصر والكلام ،ونحوها ما عدا الإرادة، وقولنا: «في إيجاد الممكن ـ إلخ» ، كفصل ثانٍ تَخْرُجُ به الإرادة، فإنَّها لا تؤثر في الإيجادِ والإعدام، وإنما تؤثر في تخصيص الممكن ببعض ما يجوز عليه كما يأتي بيانه قريبا، وهذا بناء على أنَّ التَّخصيص المذكور نوعٌ مِن التأثير ، وهو الصحيح، فإن ذهبت إلى أنَّ التخصيص ليس تأثيرا ، كانت الإرادة خارجة بالفصل الأوَّلِ ، وكان قوله : «في إيجاد الممكن وإعدامه» لبيان تعلق القدرة.
And after: know that our statement: (attribute) is like the genus in the definition, and our statement: 'by which comes about the bringing into existence of every possible thing and its annihilation' is an indication to one of the attachments (taʿalluqāt) of power called 'the eternal dispositional attachment' or 'the eternal salutary attachment', and its explanation along with the other attachments of power will come soon. And our statement: 'by it' is an indication that the effect is truly from the essence, and ascribing the effect to power is metaphorical, because power is a cause in the effect. And our statement: 'every possible thing' is a restrictive condition for exclusion, by which the necessary (wājib) and the impossible (mustaḥīl) are excluded, for these two are not things with which power attaches. That is because if it attached to the necessary, it would not be correct to annihilate it, because the necessary does not accept non-existence, nor would it be correct to bring it into existence, because in bringing it into existence there would be obtaining what is already obtained (taḥṣīl al-ḥāṣil). And if it attached to the impossible, it would not be correct to bring it into existence, because the impossible does not accept existence, nor would it be correct to annihilate it, because in annihilating it there would be obtaining what is already obtained. And the meaning of our statement: 'in accordance with will' is that everything that Allah specifies by His will He manifests by His power. So the attachment of will, being eternal, precedes the attachment of power, being temporal and incipient (ḥādith). And from this expression you understand that order exists between the attachment of the two attributes of power and will, and that there is no order between the two attributes themselves; there is no order therein. Otherwise, if it were not so, the later of the two would be incipient. And among the scholars are those who defined eternal power by his statement: 'An attribute that effects in bringing into existence the possible and annihilating it.' So his statement: (attribute) is like the genus in the definition, encompassing all attributes. And his statement: (effects) is like the first differentia, by which are excluded all attributes that have no effect, such as knowledge, life, hearing, sight, speech, and similar ones, except will. And our statement: 'in bringing into existence the possible, etc.' is like a second differentia, by which will is excluded, for it does not effect in bringing into existence and annihilation, but rather it effects in specifying the possible with some of what is permissible for it, as its explanation will come soon. And this is based on the view that the aforementioned specification is a type of effect, and that is correct. If you hold that specification is not an effect, then will is excluded by the first differentia, and his statement: 'in bringing into existence the possible and annihilating it' is for clarifying the attachment of power.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of power (qudra). The author begins by analyzing the definition phrase by phrase. The statement 'attribute' (ṣifa) acts as the genus, covering all attributes. The phrase 'by which comes about the bringing into existence of every possible thing and its annihilation' points to one particular attachment of power called the 'eternal dispositional attachment' (al-taʿalluq al-ṣalūḥī al-qadīm). The word 'by it' (bihā) indicates that the real effect comes from the essence, not from the attribute; attributing effect to power is metaphorical because power is merely a cause. The phrase 'every possible thing' (kull mumkin) is a restrictive condition that excludes the necessary (wājib) and the impossible (mustaḥīl): power cannot attach to the necessary because it cannot be annihilated (it does not accept non-existence) and bringing it into existence would be redundant, and it cannot attach to the impossible because it cannot be brought into existence (it does not accept existence). The phrase 'in accordance with will' (ʿalā wifq al-irāda) means that whatever Allah wills, He creates by His power; the attachment of will (eternal) precedes the attachment of power (temporal). From this, we deduce an order between the attachments (not the attributes themselves) because otherwise one attribute would be temporal. The author then presents an alternative definition by some scholars: 'An attribute that effects in bringing into existence the possible and annihilating it.' He shows how this definition also works: 'attribute' is the genus, 'effects' (tuʾaththir) excludes attributes like knowledge that have no effect, and 'in bringing into existence the possible, etc.' excludes will, which effects in specification (takhṣīṣ) rather than creation. The author notes that the correct view is that specification is a type of effect; if one denies that, then will is excluded by the first differentia and the second phrase merely describes the attachment of power.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Power directly creates things without the essence being the agent.
Correction: The passage states that the effect is truly from the essence, and ascribing effect to power is metaphorical because power is a cause.

Checkpoint
According to the definition, why does power not attach to the necessary (wājib)?
A) Because the necessary is not possible.
B) Because it would be impossible to annihilate it and redundant to create it.
C) Because power only attaches to contingent beings.
D) Because the necessary has no attribute.

Key Takeaway
The definition of divine power specifies that it attaches only to possible things and operates according to divine will, with the true effect belonging to the essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Knowing that Allah's power attaches only to possible things, and that He does not change His own necessary nature, how does this deepen your trust in His decree? Are there things you wish Allah would do that are actually impossible? How does this lesson help you submit to His wisdom?
?
The passage states that the effect is truly from the essence, and power is only a cause. In your life, do you sometimes attribute outcomes to secondary causes rather than to Allah? How can you train your heart to see His essence as the true agent behind every event?
?
The attachment of will is eternal, while the attachment of power is temporal. This means every event occurs exactly at the time Allah willed eternally. How does this affect your patience in waiting for relief? Do you sometimes feel your dua is not answered because you haven't seen the result? How does this lesson strengthen your certainty that His timing is perfect?

An Alternative Definition of Power and Comparison of Definitions
The author presents an alternative definition of power and compares it to the first, focusing on how it excludes will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand an alternative definition of power and how it differs from the first, especially regarding the role of will.

Core Idea
Power effects existence and annihilation, while will effects specification.

After presenting the standard definition, the author mentions that some scholars define power differently. This lesson examines that second definition and shows how it also successfully distinguishes power from other attributes, especially will. The key difference lies in whether specification is considered an effect.

Guided Path
1
Read the alternative definition
Read the passage that begins with 'Among the scholars are those who defined eternal power...' and see how it differs from the first.
This definition is simpler in form.
2
Analyze the role of 'attribute' as genus
Just like before, 'attribute' is the genus. Here 'effects' is the first differentia.
Notice the use of 'tuʾaththir' (effects) instead of the longer phrase.
3
Understand how this definition excludes other attributes
The phrase 'effects' excludes attributes like knowledge that have no effect. The phrase 'in bringing into existence the possible, etc.' excludes will, because will effects specification, not creation.
There is a subtlety: if specification is not considered an effect, will is excluded by the first differentia.
4
Compare with the first definition
Reflect on the differences: the first definition explicitly includes 'in accordance with will', while the second does not. The second treats specification as a type of effect.
The author notes that the correct view is that specification is a type of effect.

وبعد ؛ فاعلم أن قولنا: (صفة) ، كالجنس في التعريف ، وقولنا : يتأتى بها إيجاد كل ممكن وإعدامه» ، إشارة إلى تعلُّق من تعلقات القدرة يسمى: «التعلق الصَّلوحي القديم» أو «التَّعلق الصَّلَاحي القديم ، وسيأتي بيانه مع سائر تعلقات القدرة قريبا، وقولنا: «بها»، إشارة إلى أنَّ التأثير حقيقة للذات ، وإسنادُ التأثير إلى القدرة مجاز، لكون القدرة سببا في التأثير، وقولنا: «كل ممكن»، قيد للاحتراز ، يخرج به الواجب والمستحيل، فإنهما مما لا تعلق للقدرة به ، وذلك لأنها لو تعلقت بالواجب لم يصح أن تعدمه ؛ لأن الواجب لا يقبل العدم، يصح توجده ؛ لأن في إيجادها إياه تحصيل الحاصل ، ولو تعلقت بالمستحيل لم يصح أن توجده ؛ لأن المستحيل لا يقبل الوجود ، ولا يصح أن تعدمه ؛ لأنَّ في إعدامها إياه تحصيل الحاصل ، ومعنى قولنا: على وفق الإرادة» أن كل ما خصصه الله تعالى بإرادته أبرزه بقدرته ، فتعلق الإرادة لكونه أزليّاً سابق على تعلق القدرة لكونه تنجيزاً حادثًا ، ومن هذه العبارة تدرك [؟] أن الترتيب حاصل بين تعلق صفتي القدرة والإرادة ، وأنه لا ترتيب بين نفس الصفتين ؛ لا ترتيب فيه ، وإلا يكن الأمر كذلك كان المتأخّر منهما حادثا ، ومن العلماء من عرف القديم القدرة بقوله : «صفة تؤثر في إيجاد الممكن وإعدامه ، فقوله : (صفة) ، كالجنس في التعريف يشمل جميع الصفات، وقوله: (تؤثر»، كالفصل الأوَّلِ يَخْرجُ به جميع ما لا تأثير له من الصفات، كالعلم والحياة والسمع والبصر والكلام ،ونحوها ما عدا الإرادة، وقولنا: «في إيجاد الممكن ـ إلخ» ، كفصل ثانٍ تَخْرُجُ به الإرادة، فإنَّها لا تؤثر في الإيجادِ والإعدام، وإنما تؤثر في تخصيص الممكن ببعض ما يجوز عليه كما يأتي بيانه قريبا، وهذا بناء على أنَّ التَّخصيص المذكور نوعٌ مِن التأثير ، وهو الصحيح، فإن ذهبت إلى أنَّ التخصيص ليس تأثيرا ، كانت الإرادة خارجة بالفصل الأوَّلِ ، وكان قوله : «في إيجاد الممكن وإعدامه» لبيان تعلق القدرة.
And after: know that our statement: (attribute) is like the genus in the definition, and our statement: 'by which comes about the bringing into existence of every possible thing and its annihilation' is an indication to one of the attachments (taʿalluqāt) of power called 'the eternal dispositional attachment' or 'the eternal salutary attachment', and its explanation along with the other attachments of power will come soon. And our statement: 'by it' is an indication that the effect is truly from the essence, and ascribing the effect to power is metaphorical, because power is a cause in the effect. And our statement: 'every possible thing' is a restrictive condition for exclusion, by which the necessary (wājib) and the impossible (mustaḥīl) are excluded, for these two are not things with which power attaches. That is because if it attached to the necessary, it would not be correct to annihilate it, because the necessary does not accept non-existence, nor would it be correct to bring it into existence, because in bringing it into existence there would be obtaining what is already obtained (taḥṣīl al-ḥāṣil). And if it attached to the impossible, it would not be correct to bring it into existence, because the impossible does not accept existence, nor would it be correct to annihilate it, because in annihilating it there would be obtaining what is already obtained. And the meaning of our statement: 'in accordance with will' is that everything that Allah specifies by His will He manifests by His power. So the attachment of will, being eternal, precedes the attachment of power, being temporal and incipient (ḥādith). And from this expression you understand that order exists between the attachment of the two attributes of power and will, and that there is no order between the two attributes themselves; there is no order therein. Otherwise, if it were not so, the later of the two would be incipient. And among the scholars are those who defined eternal power by his statement: 'An attribute that effects in bringing into existence the possible and annihilating it.' So his statement: (attribute) is like the genus in the definition, encompassing all attributes. And his statement: (effects) is like the first differentia, by which are excluded all attributes that have no effect, such as knowledge, life, hearing, sight, speech, and similar ones, except will. And our statement: 'in bringing into existence the possible, etc.' is like a second differentia, by which will is excluded, for it does not effect in bringing into existence and annihilation, but rather it effects in specifying the possible with some of what is permissible for it, as its explanation will come soon. And this is based on the view that the aforementioned specification is a type of effect, and that is correct. If you hold that specification is not an effect, then will is excluded by the first differentia, and his statement: 'in bringing into existence the possible and annihilating it' is for clarifying the attachment of power.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of power (qudra). The author begins by analyzing the definition phrase by phrase. The statement 'attribute' (ṣifa) acts as the genus, covering all attributes. The phrase 'by which comes about the bringing into existence of every possible thing and its annihilation' points to one particular attachment of power called the 'eternal dispositional attachment' (al-taʿalluq al-ṣalūḥī al-qadīm). The word 'by it' (bihā) indicates that the real effect comes from the essence, not from the attribute; attributing effect to power is metaphorical because power is merely a cause. The phrase 'every possible thing' (kull mumkin) is a restrictive condition that excludes the necessary (wājib) and the impossible (mustaḥīl): power cannot attach to the necessary because it cannot be annihilated (it does not accept non-existence) and bringing it into existence would be redundant, and it cannot attach to the impossible because it cannot be brought into existence (it does not accept existence). The phrase 'in accordance with will' (ʿalā wifq al-irāda) means that whatever Allah wills, He creates by His power; the attachment of will (eternal) precedes the attachment of power (temporal). From this, we deduce an order between the attachments (not the attributes themselves) because otherwise one attribute would be temporal. The author then presents an alternative definition by some scholars: 'An attribute that effects in bringing into existence the possible and annihilating it.' He shows how this definition also works: 'attribute' is the genus, 'effects' (tuʾaththir) excludes attributes like knowledge that have no effect, and 'in bringing into existence the possible, etc.' excludes will, which effects in specification (takhṣīṣ) rather than creation. The author notes that the correct view is that specification is a type of effect; if one denies that, then will is excluded by the first differentia and the second phrase merely describes the attachment of power.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Specification is not a type of effect, so will is not excluded by the second definition.
Correction: The author states that the correct view is that specification is a type of effect, so will is excluded by the second differentia. If one denies that, will is excluded by the first differentia instead.

Checkpoint
According to the author's analysis, what is the role of specification (takhṣīṣ) in relation to power and will?
A) Specification is not an effect; it belongs to will.
B) Specification is a type of effect, and will effects specification.
C) Specification is the same as creation.
D) Specification is unrelated to power.

Key Takeaway
The alternative definition successfully distinguishes power from will by considering specification as an effect, or if not, by relying on the first differentia.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation where things don't go as you wished, do you attribute that to Allah's power or His will? How does the distinction in this lesson help you see that both are at work in every event?
?
The passage teaches that will effects specification, not creation. How does this truth change the way you pray for something? Are you asking Allah to bring it into existence or to specify it for you?
?
If specification is truly an effect of Allah's will, then every detail of your life is intended by Him. What small, seemingly random details of your day today do you now realize are specified by Allah's will? How does that awareness shift your gratitude?

The Definition of the Attribute of Will (Irada)
The author defines the attribute of will as an eternal attribute whose function is specification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise definition of the divine attribute of will (irada) and its distinct function of specification.

Core Idea
Will is the eternal attribute that specifies what comes to be.

In the previous lesson, we encountered the attribute of power. Now the author turns to the attribute of will (irada). This short but dense sentence lays out the essential components of the divine will: it is eternal, distinct from the essence, and its unique role is specification. Let's examine each component carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Start by reading the Arabic text and its translation. Notice the concise structure.
The passage is only one sentence, but it packs multiple components.
2
Identify the five components
Break down the definition into its parts: attribute, eternal, additional, subsisting, function. Write them down.
3
Understand specification
The key term 'takhṣīṣ' (specification) is what distinguishes will from other attributes. Consider what specification means: selecting one possibility among many.
Specification is not creation; it is the decision of what to create.
4
Distinguish will from power
Recall that power is about bringing into existence. Will decides which possible thing is brought into existence. The passage explicitly says 'specifies every possible thing'.
This distinction prevents the misconception that will and power are identical.
5
Summarize the definition
In your own words, write a complete definition of the divine will incorporating all five components.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وثانيتها (إِرَادَةٌ) وهي : صفةٌ قديمةٌ زائدة على الذات ، قائمة بها ، شَأْنُها التخصيص ؛ فتُخصص كل ممكن ببعض ما يجوز عليه
And the second [attribute] is will (irāda), and it is an eternal attribute (ṣifa qadīma), additional to the essence (zāʾida ʿalā al-dhāt), subsisting in it (qāʾima bihā), whose function (shaʾn) is specification (takhṣīṣ); so it specifies every possible thing with some of what is permissible for it.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage defines the second divine attribute: will (irāda). The definition consists of several components: it is an attribute (ṣifa), it is eternal (qadīma), it is additional to the essence (zāʾida ʿalā al-dhāt), it subsists in the essence (qāʾima bihā), and its function (shaʾn) is specification (takhṣīṣ). Specification means that will determines for each possible thing (mumkin) a particular state among all the states that are permissible for it (i.e., that are not impossible). This distinguishes will from power: power brings into existence and annihilates, while will specifies which possible thing comes into existence and in what manner. The definition is concise but comprehensive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think will and power are the same thing or that will is the same as creation.
Correction: Will is not power; power brings into existence, while will specifies which possibilities come to be. Will is the attribute of specification, not creation.

Checkpoint
What is the function (sha’n) of the attribute of will according to this definition?
A) Bringing into existence and annihilation
B) Specification of possibles
C) Knowledge of all things
D) Giving life

Key Takeaway
The attribute of will (irāda) is an eternal, essence-additional attribute whose sole function is specification (takhṣīṣ) – determining which possibilities become actual.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Since God's will is an eternal and unchanging attribute, does your trust in His decrees waver when you face unfulfilled desires? How can you actively surrender those unmet hopes to His perfect specification today?
?
The function of will is to distinguish between possibilities—God chooses one over others. In your decisions, do you often insist on your own specification of events, forgetting that His will is the ultimate decider? What is one area of your life where you need to consciously accept His specification over your preference?

Classification of the Attachments of Divine Power
Sanusi classifies the attachments of power into seven types across three categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the seven-fold classification of the attachments of divine power into one eternal dispositional, three grasp, and three executive attachments.

Core Idea
Divine power attaches to possibles in three distinct ways.

Sanusi begins by clarifying the literal and metaphorical meanings of 'attachment' before presenting the detailed classification given by the verifiers. This taxonomy is essential for understanding how God's power relates to creation in different time frames and modes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the translation. Pay attention to the terms used for each type.
2
Identify the three main categories
Find the one eternal dispositional attachment, the three grasp attachments, and the three executive attachments. Note their definitions.
The grasp attachments are about continuing states, while executive are about actual changes.
3
Compare literal vs. metaphorical attachment
The author explains that 'attachment' is literal for executive and metaphorical for disposition/grasp. Understand why.
4
Reflect on the seven types
Ask yourself: what do these seven types cover? They cover all possible states of creation and annihilation.
This will connect to the next lesson on limits of power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الكلام على تعلق القدرة: فاعلم أولا: أنَّ معنى تعلق الصفة بشيء: «اقتضاء الصفة واستلزامها أمرا زائدا على القيام بمحلها على ما سيأتي في كلام الشارح وهذا المعنى حقيقة في التعلق بالفعل وهو التنجيزي ، وأما إطلاق التّعلق على صلاحية الصفة في لشيء أو على كون الشَّيء في قبضة الصفة فهو مجاز. ثم اعلم أن أقصى ما ذكره المحققون أنَّ للقدرة تعلقات واحد منها يسمى: «التعلق الصلوحي القديم وثلاثة يسمى كل منها : تعلق «القبضة وثلاثة كل منها يسمى: «التعلق التنجيزي الحادث أما الأول ـ وهو الصلوحي القديم ـ فهو صلاحيتها في الأزل للإيجاد والإعدام فيما لا يزال، فأما تعلقات القبضة الثلاثة فهي : تعلقها بعدمنا فيما لا يزال قبل وجودنا، وتعلقها باستمرار الوجود بعد العدم، وتعلقها باستمرار العدم بعد الوجود، ومعنى ذلك أن الممكن في قبضة القدرة ، فإن شاء الله تعالى أبقاه على عدمه، أو على وجوده ، وإن شاء أوجده أو أعدمه. وأما التعلقات التنجيزية الحادثة الثلاثة فهي : تعلقها بإيجادنا بالفعل بعد العدم السابق ، وتعلقها بإعدامنا بالفعل بعد الوجود، وتعلقها بإيجادنا بالفعل حين البعث . وأما عدم الممكن فى الأزل فهذا لا تتعلق به القدرة اتفاقا ؛ لأنه واجب لا جائز ، وقد علمت أنَّ القدرة إنما تتعلق بالممكنات لا بالواجبات ، والدليل على أنها لا تتعلق بعدمنا في الأزل: أنها لو تعلقت به حينئذ لجاز وجودنا أزلا ، وهو باطل ؛ لما يلزم عليه من تعدد ذوات القدماء. وذهب الأشعري وإمام الحرمين إلى أنها لا تتعلق بإعدامنا بعد وجودنا ـ وهو أحد ما ذكرناه التعلقات التنجيزية الحادثة ، بل عند الأشعري أنه إذا أراد الله عدم الممكن قطع عنه الإمدادات فينعدم بنفسه، ونظير ذلك أنك إذا وضعت الزَّيت في السراج فإن الفَتِيلَةَ تستمر منوّرة فإذا فرغ الزَّيْتُ طفئت الفتيلة بدون فعل فاعل.
And as for the discussion on the attachment (taʿalluq) of power: know first that the meaning of the attachment of an attribute to a thing is 'the attribute's requiring and entailing something additional to its subsisting in its locus', as will come in the words of the commentator. This meaning is literal in the attachment to an act, which is the executive (al-tanjīzī). As for applying the term 'attachment' to the disposition (ṣalāḥiyya) of the attribute to a thing, or to the thing being in the grasp (qabḍa) of the attribute, it is metaphorical (majāz). Then know that the furthest the verifiers (muḥaqqiqūn) have mentioned is that power has attachments: one called 'the eternal dispositional attachment' (al-taʿalluq al-ṣalūḥī al-qadīm), three each called 'attachment of the grasp' (qabḍa), and three each called 'the temporal executive attachment' (al-taʿalluq al-tanjīzī al-ḥādith). As for the first, which is the eternal dispositional, it is its suitability (ṣalāḥiyya) in pre-eternity (azal) for bringing into existence and annihilation in what will be (mā lā yazāl). As for the three attachments of the grasp: they are its attachment to our non-existence in what will be before our existence, its attachment to the continuation of existence after non-existence, and its attachment to the continuation of non-existence after existence. The meaning of that is that the possible is in the grasp of power; if Allah wills, He keeps it in its non-existence, or in its existence, and if He wills, He brings it into existence or annihilates it. As for the three temporal executive attachments: they are its attachment to bringing us into existence actually after prior non-existence, its attachment to annihilating us actually after existence, and its attachment to bringing us into existence actually at the time of resurrection (baʿth). And as for the non-existence of the possible in pre-eternity, power does not attach to it by agreement; because it is necessary (wājib) not possible (jāʾiz), and you have known that power only attaches to possibles (mumkināt), not to necessities. The proof that it does not attach to our non-existence in pre-eternity: if it attached to it then, our existence in pre-eternity would be possible, which is false because of what would follow from it: the multiplicity of eternal entities (tʿaddud dhawāt al-qudamāʾ). And al-Ashʿarī and Imām al-Ḥaramayn held that it does not attach to our annihilation after our existence—which is one of what we mentioned as temporal executive attachments. Rather, according to al-Ashʿarī, if Allah wills the non-existence of a possible, He cuts off the supplies (imdādāt) from it, so it becomes non-existent by itself. An analogy is: if you put oil in a lamp, the wick continues to shine, and when the oil runs out, the wick goes out without any agent's action.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed classification of the attachments (taʿalluqāt) of the attribute of power. First, it defines what 'attachment of an attribute' means: it is the attribute's requiring something additional to its mere subsistence in its locus. This is true in the literal sense for the executive attachment (taʿalluq tanjīzī), while applying it to the attribute's disposition or to the thing being in its grasp is metaphorical. Then the author enumerates seven types according to the verifiers: one eternal dispositional attachment (al-ṣalūḥī al-qadīm) – the attribute's suitability for creation and annihilation in the future; three 'grasp' attachments (qabḍa) – power's relation to our non-existence prior to existence, to the continuation of existence after non-existence, and to the continuation of non-existence after existence; and three temporal executive attachments (tanjīzī ḥādith) – the actual bringing into existence after non-existence, actual annihilation after existence, and actual resurrection. He then clarifies a point of agreement: power does not attach to the non-existence of the possible in pre-eternity because that non-existence is necessary (it must be that the possible is non-existent before its creation), and power only attaches to possibles. The proof: if it attached, our existence in pre-eternity would be possible, leading to an impossible multiplicity of eternal beings. Finally, the author notes a disagreement: al-Ashʿarī and Imām al-Ḥaramayn hold that power does not directly effect annihilation after existence; rather, God cuts off sustaining supports, and the thing ceases to exist by itself. An analogy is given: a lamp wick goes out when the oil finishes, without a new act of extinguishing.

Key Terms
تعلق
القدرة
التعلق الصلوحي القديم
تعلق القبضة
التعلق التنجيزي الحادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All attachments of power are direct acts of creation or annihilation.
Correction: The passage explains that attachment can be metaphorical for disposition or grasp, not only executive.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many attachments of power are mentioned in total (excluding sub-classifications)?
A) Three
B) Five
C) Seven
D) Nine

Key Takeaway
Divine power attaches to possibles in seven ways, covering all states before, during, and after existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's power attaches to your non-existence before you existed, meaning He could have kept you in non-existence, what does that reveal about your entitlement to exist? How does this realization change the way you view your life as a gift from Him, and what will you do today to show gratitude for being brought into existence?
?
The grasp attachments include God's power to continue your existence after you come into being. Do you recognize that every breath you take is only because He wills to sustain you? What would change in your daily routine if you truly internalized that at any moment He could 'keep you in non-existence'? Are you living in a way that would be meaningful if your existence ended now?
?
The executive attachment of resurrection (baʿth) means God's power will bring you back to life for judgment. If you were judged right now based on your current state of faith and actions, what verdict would you expect? How does the certainty of this future attachment of power compel you to prepare for that day starting today?

The Scope of Power: Consensus and Disagreement on Annihilation
Sanusi discusses the consensus that power does not attach to pre-eternal non-existence and the disagreement on annihilation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why power does not attach to the non-existence of the possible in pre-eternity and the Ashʿarī position that annihilation is indirect.

Core Idea
Power only attaches to possibles, and annihilation can occur by cutting off support.

After classifying the attachments, Sanusi clarifies an important limit: power does not attach to the non-existence of the possible in pre-eternity, as that is necessary. He also presents a significant disagreement regarding whether power directly annihilates.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Notice the shift from consensus to disagreement.
2
Understand the proof
The passage gives a proof: if power attached to pre-eternal non-existence, the possible could be eternal, leading to multiple eternal entities. This is impossible.
Think about why multiple eternal entities are impossible.
3
Identify the Ashʿarī position
Al-Ashʿarī and Imām al-Ḥaramayn held that power does not directly annihilate; instead, God cuts off supplies.
4
Reflect on the analogy
The lamp analogy shows that cessation can occur without a direct act. How does this affect our understanding of divine power?
This analogy is key to the Ashʿarī view.

وأما الكلام على تعلق القدرة: فاعلم أولا: أنَّ معنى تعلق الصفة بشيء: «اقتضاء الصفة واستلزامها أمرا زائدا على القيام بمحلها على ما سيأتي في كلام الشارح وهذا المعنى حقيقة في التعلق بالفعل وهو التنجيزي ، وأما إطلاق التّعلق على صلاحية الصفة في لشيء أو على كون الشَّيء في قبضة الصفة فهو مجاز. ثم اعلم أن أقصى ما ذكره المحققون أنَّ للقدرة تعلقات واحد منها يسمى: «التعلق الصلوحي القديم وثلاثة يسمى كل منها : تعلق «القبضة وثلاثة كل منها يسمى: «التعلق التنجيزي الحادث أما الأول ـ وهو الصلوحي القديم ـ فهو صلاحيتها في الأزل للإيجاد والإعدام فيما لا يزال، فأما تعلقات القبضة الثلاثة فهي : تعلقها بعدمنا فيما لا يزال قبل وجودنا، وتعلقها باستمرار الوجود بعد العدم، وتعلقها باستمرار العدم بعد الوجود، ومعنى ذلك أن الممكن في قبضة القدرة ، فإن شاء الله تعالى أبقاه على عدمه، أو على وجوده ، وإن شاء أوجده أو أعدمه. وأما التعلقات التنجيزية الحادثة الثلاثة فهي : تعلقها بإيجادنا بالفعل بعد العدم السابق ، وتعلقها بإعدامنا بالفعل بعد الوجود، وتعلقها بإيجادنا بالفعل حين البعث . وأما عدم الممكن فى الأزل فهذا لا تتعلق به القدرة اتفاقا ؛ لأنه واجب لا جائز ، وقد علمت أنَّ القدرة إنما تتعلق بالممكنات لا بالواجبات ، والدليل على أنها لا تتعلق بعدمنا في الأزل: أنها لو تعلقت به حينئذ لجاز وجودنا أزلا ، وهو باطل ؛ لما يلزم عليه من تعدد ذوات القدماء. وذهب الأشعري وإمام الحرمين إلى أنها لا تتعلق بإعدامنا بعد وجودنا ـ وهو أحد ما ذكرناه التعلقات التنجيزية الحادثة ، بل عند الأشعري أنه إذا أراد الله عدم الممكن قطع عنه الإمدادات فينعدم بنفسه، ونظير ذلك أنك إذا وضعت الزَّيت في السراج فإن الفَتِيلَةَ تستمر منوّرة فإذا فرغ الزَّيْتُ طفئت الفتيلة بدون فعل فاعل.
And as for the discussion on the attachment (taʿalluq) of power: know first that the meaning of the attachment of an attribute to a thing is 'the attribute's requiring and entailing something additional to its subsisting in its locus', as will come in the words of the commentator. This meaning is literal in the attachment to an act, which is the executive (al-tanjīzī). As for applying the term 'attachment' to the disposition (ṣalāḥiyya) of the attribute to a thing, or to the thing being in the grasp (qabḍa) of the attribute, it is metaphorical (majāz). Then know that the furthest the verifiers (muḥaqqiqūn) have mentioned is that power has attachments: one called 'the eternal dispositional attachment' (al-taʿalluq al-ṣalūḥī al-qadīm), three each called 'attachment of the grasp' (qabḍa), and three each called 'the temporal executive attachment' (al-taʿalluq al-tanjīzī al-ḥādith). As for the first, which is the eternal dispositional, it is its suitability (ṣalāḥiyya) in pre-eternity (azal) for bringing into existence and annihilation in what will be (mā lā yazāl). As for the three attachments of the grasp: they are its attachment to our non-existence in what will be before our existence, its attachment to the continuation of existence after non-existence, and its attachment to the continuation of non-existence after existence. The meaning of that is that the possible is in the grasp of power; if Allah wills, He keeps it in its non-existence, or in its existence, and if He wills, He brings it into existence or annihilates it. As for the three temporal executive attachments: they are its attachment to bringing us into existence actually after prior non-existence, its attachment to annihilating us actually after existence, and its attachment to bringing us into existence actually at the time of resurrection (baʿth). And as for the non-existence of the possible in pre-eternity, power does not attach to it by agreement; because it is necessary (wājib) not possible (jāʾiz), and you have known that power only attaches to possibles (mumkināt), not to necessities. The proof that it does not attach to our non-existence in pre-eternity: if it attached to it then, our existence in pre-eternity would be possible, which is false because of what would follow from it: the multiplicity of eternal entities (tʿaddud dhawāt al-qudamāʾ). And al-Ashʿarī and Imām al-Ḥaramayn held that it does not attach to our annihilation after our existence—which is one of what we mentioned as temporal executive attachments. Rather, according to al-Ashʿarī, if Allah wills the non-existence of a possible, He cuts off the supplies (imdādāt) from it, so it becomes non-existent by itself. An analogy is: if you put oil in a lamp, the wick continues to shine, and when the oil runs out, the wick goes out without any agent's action.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed classification of the attachments (taʿalluqāt) of the attribute of power. First, it defines what 'attachment of an attribute' means: it is the attribute's requiring something additional to its mere subsistence in its locus. This is true in the literal sense for the executive attachment (taʿalluq tanjīzī), while applying it to the attribute's disposition or to the thing being in its grasp is metaphorical. Then the author enumerates seven types according to the verifiers: one eternal dispositional attachment (al-ṣalūḥī al-qadīm) – the attribute's suitability for creation and annihilation in the future; three 'grasp' attachments (qabḍa) – power's relation to our non-existence prior to existence, to the continuation of existence after non-existence, and to the continuation of non-existence after existence; and three temporal executive attachments (tanjīzī ḥādith) – the actual bringing into existence after non-existence, actual annihilation after existence, and actual resurrection. He then clarifies a point of agreement: power does not attach to the non-existence of the possible in pre-eternity because that non-existence is necessary (it must be that the possible is non-existent before its creation), and power only attaches to possibles. The proof: if it attached, our existence in pre-eternity would be possible, leading to an impossible multiplicity of eternal beings. Finally, the author notes a disagreement: al-Ashʿarī and Imām al-Ḥaramayn hold that power does not directly effect annihilation after existence; rather, God cuts off sustaining supports, and the thing ceases to exist by itself. An analogy is given: a lamp wick goes out when the oil finishes, without a new act of extinguishing.

Key Terms
الأزل
الممكن
الواجب
الإمدادات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Power directly annihilates by a specific act.
Correction: The Ashʿarī view is that annihilation occurs by cutting off support, not a direct act.

Checkpoint
According to the consensus, why does power not attach to the non-existence of the possible in pre-eternity?
A) Because it is impossible
B) Because it is necessary
C) Because it is possible
D) Because it is eternal

Key Takeaway
The attachment of divine power is limited to possible entities in contingent states, and annihilation is understood as cessation of support rather than a direct act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your entire existence depends on God's continuous support like the lamp depends on oil, how does that change the way you view your own abilities and achievements? What practical step can you take today to acknowledge that dependence?
?
The proof shows that God's power cannot attach to what is impossible. Are there things in your life that you find yourself expecting from God that are actually impossible? How can you align your expectations with what is truly possible?
?
The Ash'ari view says that when God cuts off support, a thing ceases by itself. In what areas of your spiritual life are you still trying to 'extinguish' your own bad habits through your own effort, rather than asking God to cut off the support that keeps them alive?

Divine Attributes

The Meaning of Attribute Relation
The author defines the meaning of attribute relation and distinguishes literal from metaphorical usage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the term 'relation' (ta`alluq) of an attribute has a literal meaning (actualizing relation) and a metaphorical meaning (fitness and grasp).

Core Idea
Relation is literal for action, metaphorical for potential and possession.

Before exploring the specific types of relations of divine power, it's essential to grasp what 'relation' of an attribute means. The author clarifies that this term is not used uniformly. This lesson establishes the foundational distinction between literal and metaphorical usage, preventing misunderstandings later.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of 'relation'
Read the opening where the author defines ta‘alluq as the attribute's requiring an extra matter beyond subsisting in its locus.
Notice that this definition emphasizes an 'extra matter' — the relation is something additional.
2
Identify the literal vs metaphorical usage
The author states that the definition applies literally to the actualizing relation (al-tanjīzī), but when applied to fitness (ṣulūḥī) or grasp (qabḍa), it is metaphorical.
This distinction is crucial for understanding later classifications.
3
Reflect on why this matters
Consider how using the same word for different types could cause confusion if the distinction is not clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الكلام على تعلق القدرة: فاعلم أولا: أنَّ معنى تعلق الصفة بشيء: «اقتضاء الصفة واستلزامها أمرا زائدا على القيام بمحلها على ما سيأتي في كلام الشارح وهذا المعنى حقيقة في التعلق بالفعل وهو التنجيزي ، وأما إطلاق التّعلق على صلاحية الصفة في لشيء أو على كون الشَّيء في قبضة الصفة فهو مجاز. ثم اعلم أن أقصى ما ذكره المحققون أنَّ للقدرة تعلقات واحد منها يسمى: «التعلق الصلوحي القديم وثلاثة يسمى كل منها : تعلق «القبضة وثلاثة كل منها يسمى: «التعلق التنجيزي الحادث أما الأول ـ وهو الصلوحي القديم ـ فهو صلاحيتها في الأزل للإيجاد والإعدام فيما لا يزال، فأما تعلقات القبضة الثلاثة فهي : تعلقها بعدمنا فيما لا يزال قبل وجودنا، وتعلقها باستمرار الوجود بعد العدم، وتعلقها باستمرار العدم بعد الوجود، ومعنى ذلك أن الممكن في قبضة القدرة ، فإن شاء الله تعالى أبقاه على عدمه، أو على وجوده ، وإن شاء أوجده أو أعدمه. وأما التعلقات التنجيزية الحادثة الثلاثة فهي : تعلقها بإيجادنا بالفعل بعد العدم السابق ، وتعلقها بإعدامنا بالفعل بعد الوجود، وتعلقها بإيجادنا بالفعل حين البعث . وأما عدم الممكن فى الأزل فهذا لا تتعلق به القدرة اتفاقا ؛ لأنه واجب لا جائز ، وقد علمت أنَّ القدرة إنما تتعلق بالممكنات لا بالواجبات ، والدليل على أنها لا تتعلق بعدمنا في الأزل: أنها لو تعلقت به حينئذ لجاز وجودنا أزلا ، وهو باطل ؛ لما يلزم عليه من تعدد ذوات القدماء. وذهب الأشعري وإمام الحرمين إلى أنها لا تتعلق بإعدامنا بعد وجودنا ـ وهو أحد ما ذكرناه التعلقات التنجيزية الحادثة ، بل عند الأشعري أنه إذا أراد الله عدم الممكن قطع عنه الإمدادات فينعدم بنفسه، ونظير ذلك أنك إذا وضعت الزَّيت في السراج فإن الفَتِيلَةَ تستمر منوّرة فإذا فرغ الزَّيْتُ طفئت الفتيلة بدون فعل فاعل.
As for the discussion on the relation (ta‘alluq) of power (al-qudra): know first that the meaning of the relation of an attribute to something is 'the attribute's requiring and entailing an additional matter beyond subsisting in its locus' as will come in the commentator's speech. And this meaning is literal in the relation to an act, which is the actualizing relation (al-tanjīzī). As for applying the term 'relation' to the attribute's fitness for something or to the thing being in the grasp (qabḍa) of the attribute, it is metaphorical. Then know that the utmost that the verifying scholars (al-muḥaqqiqūn) have mentioned is that power has relations: one of them is called 'the fitness-relation, the eternal' (al-ta‘alluq al-ṣulūḥī al-qadīm), three each called 'grasp relation' (ta‘alluq al-qabḍa), and three each called 'the actualizing relation, the temporal' (al-ta‘alluq al-tanjīzī al-ḥādith). As for the first—the eternal fitness-relation—it is its fitness in pre-eternity for bringing into existence and annihilating in what is yet to come. As for the three grasp relations: they are its relation to our non-existence in what is yet to come before our existence, its relation to the continuance of existence after non-existence, and its relation to the continuance of non-existence after existence. The meaning of that is that the possible is in the grasp of power; if Allah wills, He keeps it in its non-existence or its existence, and if He wills, He brings it into existence or annihilates it. As for the three temporal actualizing relations: they are its relation to bringing us into existence actually after prior non-existence, its relation to annihilating us actually after existence, and its relation to bringing us into existence actually at the time of resurrection. As for the non-existence of the possible in pre-eternity, power does not relate to it by consensus, because it is necessary (wājib) not permissible (jā’iz); and you have learned that power only relates to possibles, not to necessarys. The proof that it does not relate to our non-existence in pre-eternity: if it related to it at that time, then our existence in pre-eternity would be possible, which is false because it would entail multiplicity of eternal beings (tā‘addud dhāt al-qudamā’). And al-Ash‘arī and Imām al-Ḥaramayn held that it does not relate to our annihilation after our existence—that being one of what we mentioned of the temporal actualizing relations—rather, according to al-Ash‘arī, when Allah wills the non-existence of a possible, He cuts off the supplies (al-imdādāt) from it, and it becomes non-existent by itself. An analogy for that is that if you put oil in a lamp, the wick continues to be illuminated, and when the oil runs out, the wick goes out without an agent's act.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the types of relation (ta‘alluq) of the divine attribute of power (al-qudra). The author first defines the meaning of an attribute's relation: it is the attribute's requiring an extra matter beyond its subsistence in the subject. This meaning applies literally to actual relations (al-tanjīzī), while applying the term to mere fitness (ṣulūḥī) or possession (qabḍa) is metaphorical. Next, the author presents the classification from the verifying scholars: power has seven relations—one eternal fitness-relation, three 'grasp' relations, and three temporal actualizing relations. The eternal fitness-relation is power's fitness from eternity to create or annihilate in the future. The three grasp relations involve the possible being in power's 'grasp': power relates to our non-existence before we exist, to the continuance of existence after non-existence, and to the continuance of non-existence after existence—meaning that the possible is under power's control and can be kept in either state or changed. The three temporal actualizing relations are the actual acts: bringing us into existence after non-existence, annihilating us after existence, and resurrecting us. The author then explains that power does not relate to the non-existence of a possible in pre-eternity (i.e., the state before anything is created) because that non-existence is necessary (since it would entail existence in pre-eternity, which is impossible due to multiplicity of eternal beings). The proof is that if power related to that non-existence, it would imply our existence in pre-eternity, leading to multiple eternal entities—an absurdity. Finally, the author mentions the view of al-Ash‘arī and Imām al-Ḥaramayn that power does not relate to annihilation after existence; rather, annihilation occurs by God cutting off sustaining existence, like a lamp extinguishing when the oil runs out without a direct act.

تعلق
القدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the term 'relation' (ta‘alluq) is always used in the same sense for all types of divine power relations.
Correction: The author clarifies that it is literal only for actual acts; for fitness and grasp it is metaphorical.

Checkpoint
According to the author, when is the term 'relation' (ta‘alluq) used metaphorically?
A) When it refers to an actual act of creation
B) When it refers to the attribute's fitness for something or the thing being in its grasp
C) When it refers to the attribute's subsistence in its locus
D) It is never metaphorical

Key Takeaway
Relation is literal only for actual acts; fitness and grasp are metaphorical.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of God's power in your life, do you only recognize it when something actually happens, or do you also trust in His power's 'fitness' to act even when nothing changes? Which recognition deepens your reliance on Him?
?
The author says literal relation is only for actual acts. How does this distinction affect the way you speak about God's attributes in your dua? Do you ever describe God's power in ways that might be more metaphorical than literal? Commit to adjusting one phrase in your dua tonight to be more precise.
?
If you only think of God's power in relation to things that have already happened, what might you be missing about His constant capacity to act? How can you train your heart to live in the reality of both God's actual and potential relation to your affairs?

Divine Attributes

The Seven Relations of Divine Power
The author enumerates the seven relations of divine power with definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classification of the seven relations of power: one eternal fitness-relation, three grasp relations, and three actualizing relations.

Core Idea
Divine power relates to possibles in seven distinct ways, from eternal fitness to actual acts.

The verifying scholars have identified seven relations of divine power. These cover the eternal potential, the ongoing control, and the specific acts of creation, annihilation, and resurrection. This lesson presents each category with its key features.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall classification
The author states that power has seven relations: one eternal fitness-relation, three grasp relations, and three actualizing relations.
Memorize the numbers: 1 + 3 + 3 = 7.
2
Understand the eternal fitness-relation
This is power's fitness in pre-eternity to bring into existence or annihilate in the future.
It is a potential, not an actual act.
3
Learn the three grasp relations
They relate to the possible being in power's 'grasp': before existence, continuance of existence, and continuance of non-existence.
These express God's control over the possible state.
4
Learn the three actualizing relations
They are the actual acts: creating, annihilating, and resurrecting.
These are literal relations.
