The author first defines the meaning of an attribute's relation: it is the attribute's requiring an extra matter beyond its subsistence in the subject. This meaning applies literally to actual relations (al-tanjīzī), while applying the term to mere fitness (ṣulūḥī) or possession (qabḍa) is metaphorical. Next, the author presents the classification from the verifying scholars: power has seven relations—one eternal fitness-relation, three 'grasp' relations, and three temporal actualizing relations. The eternal fitness-relation is power's fitness from eternity to create or annihilate in the future. The three grasp relations involve the possible being in power's 'grasp': power relates to our non-existence before we exist, to the continuance of existence after non-existence, and to the continuance of non-existence after existence—meaning that the possible is under power's control and can be kept in either state or changed. The three temporal actualizing relations are the actual acts: bringing us into existence after non-existence, annihilating us after existence, and resurrecting us. The author then explains that power does not relate to the non-existence of a possible in pre-eternity (i.e., the state before anything is created) because that non-existence is necessary (since it would entail existence in pre-eternity, which is impossible due to multiplicity of eternal beings). The proof is that if power related to that non-existence, it would imply our existence in pre-eternity, leading to multiple eternal entities—an absurdity. Finally, the author mentions the view of al-Ash‘arī and Imām al-Ḥaramayn that power does not relate to annihilation after existence; rather, annihilation occurs by God cutting off sustaining existence, like a lamp extinguishing when the oil runs out without a direct act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

What would change if you truly lived with the awareness that your very existence is upheld by His power moment by moment?
?
The third actualizing relation is resurrection—your being brought back to life after death. Are you living today as if that moment is certain and near? What are you doing now that you would be ashamed to face on that day?
?
God's power has an eternal fitness relation—He could have brought you into existence at any time or not at all. He chose to create you now, in this time and place. What does that say about His purpose for you? What is He calling you to do that only you can do?

The Limits of Power's Relation: Pre-Eternal Non-Existence and Ash'ari's View
The author explains the consensus that power does not relate to pre-eternal non-existence and presents al-Ash'ari's view on annihilation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why divine power does not relate to the pre-eternal non-existence of possibles, and the Ash'ari view that annihilation occurs by cutting off sustenance rather than a direct relation of power.

Core Idea
Power does not relate to necessary non-existence; annihilation occurs by cutting off sustenance.

After detailing the seven relations, the author addresses two important qualifications. First, power does not relate to the pre-eternal non-existence of possibles because that non-existence is necessary (not possible). Second, according to al-Ash‘arī and Imām al-Ḥaramayn, annihilation after existence is not a direct actualizing relation; rather, God cuts off the supplies (imdādāt) that sustain existence, and the thing ceases to exist by itself. This lesson explains the reasoning and the analogy of the lamp.

Guided Path
1
Understand the consensus on pre-eternal non-existence
The author states that power does not relate to the non-existence of a possible in pre-eternity by consensus, because that non-existence is necessary (wājib) not permissible (jā’iz).
If it were not necessary, it could have been otherwise, leading to multiplicity of eternal beings.
2
Follow the proof by contradiction
If power related to that non-existence, then existence in pre-eternity would be possible, which would require multiple eternal beings—absurd.
This proof shows why the non-existence is necessary.
3
Learn the Ash'ari view on annihilation
Al-Ash‘arī and Imām al-Ḥaramayn hold that power does not relate to annihilation after existence. Instead, God cuts off supplies, and the thing ceases naturally.
The analogy of the lamp illustrates this: when oil runs out, the wick extinguishes without an agent's act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الكلام على تعلق القدرة: فاعلم أولا: أنَّ معنى تعلق الصفة بشيء: «اقتضاء الصفة واستلزامها أمرا زائدا على القيام بمحلها على ما سيأتي في كلام الشارح وهذا المعنى حقيقة في التعلق بالفعل وهو التنجيزي ، وأما إطلاق التّعلق على صلاحية الصفة في لشيء أو على كون الشَّيء في قبضة الصفة فهو مجاز. ثم اعلم أن أقصى ما ذكره المحققون أنَّ للقدرة تعلقات واحد منها يسمى: «التعلق الصلوحي القديم وثلاثة يسمى كل منها : تعلق «القبضة وثلاثة كل منها يسمى: «التعلق التنجيزي الحادث أما الأول ـ وهو الصلوحي القديم ـ فهو صلاحيتها في الأزل للإيجاد والإعدام فيما لا يزال، فأما تعلقات القبضة الثلاثة فهي : تعلقها بعدمنا فيما لا يزال قبل وجودنا، وتعلقها باستمرار الوجود بعد العدم، وتعلقها باستمرار العدم بعد الوجود، ومعنى ذلك أن الممكن في قبضة القدرة ، فإن شاء الله تعالى أبقاه على عدمه، أو على وجوده ، وإن شاء أوجده أو أعدمه. وأما التعلقات التنجيزية الحادثة الثلاثة فهي : تعلقها بإيجادنا بالفعل بعد العدم السابق ، وتعلقها بإعدامنا بالفعل بعد الوجود، وتعلقها بإيجادنا بالفعل حين البعث . وأما عدم الممكن فى الأزل فهذا لا تتعلق به القدرة اتفاقا ؛ لأنه واجب لا جائز ، وقد علمت أنَّ القدرة إنما تتعلق بالممكنات لا بالواجبات ، والدليل على أنها لا تتعلق بعدمنا في الأزل: أنها لو تعلقت به حينئذ لجاز وجودنا أزلا ، وهو باطل ؛ لما يلزم عليه من تعدد ذوات القدماء. وذهب الأشعري وإمام الحرمين إلى أنها لا تتعلق بإعدامنا بعد وجودنا ـ وهو أحد ما ذكرناه التعلقات التنجيزية الحادثة ، بل عند الأشعري أنه إذا أراد الله عدم الممكن قطع عنه الإمدادات فينعدم بنفسه، ونظير ذلك أنك إذا وضعت الزَّيت في السراج فإن الفَتِيلَةَ تستمر منوّرة فإذا فرغ الزَّيْتُ طفئت الفتيلة بدون فعل فاعل.
As for the discussion on the relation (ta‘alluq) of power (al-qudra): know first that the meaning of the relation of an attribute to something is 'the attribute's requiring and entailing an additional matter beyond subsisting in its locus' as will come in the commentator's speech. And this meaning is literal in the relation to an act, which is the actualizing relation (al-tanjīzī). As for applying the term 'relation' to the attribute's fitness for something or to the thing being in the grasp (qabḍa) of the attribute, it is metaphorical. Then know that the utmost that the verifying scholars (al-muḥaqqiqūn) have mentioned is that power has relations: one of them is called 'the fitness-relation, the eternal' (al-ta‘alluq al-ṣulūḥī al-qadīm), three each called 'grasp relation' (ta‘alluq al-qabḍa), and three each called 'the actualizing relation, the temporal' (al-ta‘alluq al-tanjīzī al-ḥādith). As for the first—the eternal fitness-relation—it is its fitness in pre-eternity for bringing into existence and annihilating in what is yet to come. As for the three grasp relations: they are its relation to our non-existence in what is yet to come before our existence, its relation to the continuance of existence after non-existence, and its relation to the continuance of non-existence after existence. The meaning of that is that the possible is in the grasp of power; if Allah wills, He keeps it in its non-existence or its existence, and if He wills, He brings it into existence or annihilates it. As for the three temporal actualizing relations: they are its relation to bringing us into existence actually after prior non-existence, its relation to annihilating us actually after existence, and its relation to bringing us into existence actually at the time of resurrection. As for the non-existence of the possible in pre-eternity, power does not relate to it by consensus, because it is necessary (wājib) not permissible (jā’iz); and you have learned that power only relates to possibles, not to necessarys. The proof that it does not relate to our non-existence in pre-eternity: if it related to it at that time, then our existence in pre-eternity would be possible, which is false because it would entail multiplicity of eternal beings (tā‘addud dhāt al-qudamā’). And al-Ash‘arī and Imām al-Ḥaramayn held that it does not relate to our annihilation after our existence—that being one of what we mentioned of the temporal actualizing relations—rather, according to al-Ash‘arī, when Allah wills the non-existence of a possible, He cuts off the supplies (al-imdādāt) from it, and it becomes non-existent by itself. An analogy for that is that if you put oil in a lamp, the wick continues to be illuminated, and when the oil runs out, the wick goes out without an agent's act.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the types of relation (ta‘alluq) of the divine attribute of power (al-qudra). The author first defines the meaning of an attribute's relation: it is the attribute's requiring an extra matter beyond its subsistence in the subject. This meaning applies literally to actual relations (al-tanjīzī), while applying the term to mere fitness (ṣulūḥī) or possession (qabḍa) is metaphorical. Next, the author presents the classification from the verifying scholars: power has seven relations—one eternal fitness-relation, three 'grasp' relations, and three temporal actualizing relations. The eternal fitness-relation is power's fitness from eternity to create or annihilate in the future. The three grasp relations involve the possible being in power's 'grasp': power relates to our non-existence before we exist, to the continuance of existence after non-existence, and to the continuance of non-existence after existence—meaning that the possible is under power's control and can be kept in either state or changed. The three temporal actualizing relations are the actual acts: bringing us into existence after non-existence, annihilating us after existence, and resurrecting us. The author then explains that power does not relate to the non-existence of a possible in pre-eternity (i.e., the state before anything is created) because that non-existence is necessary (since it would entail existence in pre-eternity, which is impossible due to multiplicity of eternal beings). The proof is that if power related to that non-existence, it would imply our existence in pre-eternity, leading to multiple eternal entities—an absurdity. Finally, the author mentions the view of al-Ash‘arī and Imām al-Ḥaramayn that power does not relate to annihilation after existence; rather, annihilation occurs by God cutting off sustaining existence, like a lamp extinguishing when the oil runs out without a direct act.

The Definition of Divine Will (al-Irāda) and Its Components
The author defines the divine will linguistically and technically, explaining each component and its refutational role.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the technical definition of the divine will as an eternal, additional, subsisting attribute that specifies possibilities, and the deviant views it refutes.

Core Idea
The divine will is a distinct eternal attribute that actively specifies what will exist.

This lesson unpacks the precise definition of Allah's will as formulated by Sunni theologians. The definition is carefully constructed to refute several deviant views, as each component addresses a specific error. We will see how the author uses the definition as a tool for both positive teaching and polemics.

Guided Path
1
Read the linguistic and technical definition
Read the first part of the passage where the author gives the linguistic meaning (al-qaṣd) and then the technical definition of will as an eternal, additional, subsisting attribute that specifies the possible.
2
Examine each component and the group it refutes
The definition has four main components: 'attribute' (genus), 'eternal' (refutes Karramiyya), 'additional to essence' (refutes some Mu'tazila), 'subsisting in Him' (refutes two Mu'tazili groups). Note the specific groups and their errors.
The 'subsisting' component refutes al-Jubbā'ī (attribute without locus) and al-Najjār (negative attribute).
3
Understand the eternal determinative specification
The phrase 'specifies the possible by some of what is permissible for it' refers to Allah's eternal determination (al-ta'alluq al-tanjīzī al-qadīm). This is the core function of will: giving preponderance to one possibility over another.
This will be elaborated in later aspects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الكلام على هذه الصفة من الجهة الأولى فنقول: الإرادة في اللغة: القصد، وتُرادفها المشيئة ، وهي في اصطلاح علماء الكلام: صفة أزليَّة زائدة على الذات ، قائمة به سبحانه ، تُخَصِّصُ الممكن ببعض ما يجوز عليه ، فقولنا : (صفة) ، كالجنس في التعريف يشمل جميع الصفات، وقولنا: (قديمة) يراد بها الرَّدُّ على نحو الكرَّامية الذين قالوا: إنّ الإرادة صفة حادثة قائمة بذاته تعالى ، تقدَّسَ الله عما يقول المبطلون ، وقولنا : «زائدة على الذات»، يراد به الرَّدُّ على بعض المعتزلة الذين قالوا: إن الإرادة نفس الذات ، وقولنا: «قائمة بذاته تعالى» ، رد على فريقين من المعتزلة ، أولهما الجُبَّائي ومَن ذهب مذهبه من الذين قالوا: إنَّ الإرادة صفة قائمة بغير محلّ ، وثانيهما النَّجَّار ومَن ذهب مذهبه مِن الذين قالوا: إن الإرادة صفة سلبية ، وفسَّروها بأنَّها: عدم كون الفاعل ساهيًا أو مكرها ، وقد علمت فيما سبق أن الصفة السَّلبيَّة لا قيام لها ، لكونها أمرًا عدميًّا ، وقولنا: «تخصص الممكن ببعض ما يجوز عليه»، إشارة إلى التعلق التنجيزي القديم، وهو تخصيص الله تعالى الشيء أزلا بالصفات التي يعلم يوجد عليها في الخارج، وستعرفه مع سائر تعلقات الإرادة في الجهة الثالثة، وبعضهم عرف الإرادة بأنها: صفة تؤثر في اختصاص أحد طرفي الممكن، من وجود أو عدم، أو طول أو قصر ونحوها، بالوقوع بدلا عن مقابله، فقوله: «صفة»، كالجنس في التعريف أنه شامل لجميع الصَّفات، وقوله: «تؤثر»، كالفصل خرج به ما لا يؤثر مِن الصفات ، كالعلم والكلام والسمع والبصر والحياة ونحوها، ما عدا القدرة فإنها لا تخرج بهذا القيد، وقوله: «في اختصاص» ، كفصل ثان خرج به القدرة ، والمراد بتخصيص أحد طرفي الممكن بالوقوع: ترجيح وقوع أحد طرفيه.
As for the discussion on this attribute from the first aspect, we say: al-Irāda (the will) in language is intent (al-qaṣd), and it is synonymous with al-mashī’a (the wish). In the terminology of the scholars of kalām, it is: an eternal attribute (ṣifa azaliyya), additional (zā’ida) to the essence (al-dhāt), subsisting (qā’ima) in Him, may He be exalted, which specifies (tukhaṣṣiṣ) the possible (al-mumkin) by some of what is permissible for it. So our saying: (attribute) – like the genus (al-jins) in the definition – includes all attributes. And our saying: (eternal) intended by it is the refutation of the Karramiyya group who said that the will is a temporal attribute (ṣifa ḥāditha) subsisting in His essence, exalted – exalted is Allah above what the falsifiers say. And our saying: (additional to the essence) intended by it is the refutation of some Mu‘tazila who said that the will is the essence itself. And our saying: (subsisting in His essence, exalted) is a refutation of two groups of the Mu‘tazila: the first is al-Jubbā’ī and those who follow his school who said that the will is an attribute subsisting without a locus; the second is al-Najjār and those who follow his school who said that the will is a negative attribute (ṣifa salbiyya) and interpreted it as: the agent not being negligent or coerced. You have previously learned that the negative attribute has no subsistence, because it is a non–existent matter. And our saying: (which specifies the possible by some of what is permissible for it) is an indication of the eternal determinative specification (al-ta‘alluq al-tanjīzī al-qadīm), which is Allah’s specifying the thing eternally with the attributes upon which He knows it will exist externally. And you will know it along with the other relations of the will in the third aspect. And some defined the will as: an attribute that effects in the specification of one of the two sides of the possible, whether existence or non–existence, or length or shortness and the like, to occur instead of its opposite. So his saying: (attribute) – like the genus in the definition – is that it encompasses all attributes. And his saying: (effects) – like the differentia (al-faṣl) – excludes by it what does not effect of the attributes, such as knowledge, speech, hearing, sight, life and the like, except for power (al-qudra) for it is not excluded by this restriction. And his saying: (in specification) – like a second differentia – excludes by it power (al-qudra). And what is intended by specifying one of the two sides of the possible to occur is: giving preponderance (tarjīḥ) to the occurrence of one of its two sides.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the divine attribute of will (al-irāda). The author begins by giving the linguistic meaning: al-irāda is al-qaṣd (intent), and it is synonymous with al-mashī’a (wish). In kalam terminology, it is defined as an eternal attribute, additional to the essence, subsisting in Allah, that specifies a possible thing by some of what is permissible for it. The author then systematically explains each part of the definition. 'Attribute' is the genus, covering all attributes. 'Eternal' refutes the Karramiyya who held will to be temporal. 'Additional to the essence' refutes the Mu‘tazila who identified will with the essence itself. 'Subsisting in His essence' refutes two Mu‘tazili groups: al-Jubbā’ī and his followers, who said will subsists without a locus, and al-Najjār, who said will is a negative attribute (that the agent is not negligent or coerced). The statement 'specifies the possible by some of what is permissible for it' refers to the eternal determinative specification (al-ta‘alluq al-tanjīzī al-qadīm), i.e., Allah’s eternal determination of what will exist. The author then presents an alternative definition by some scholars: will is an attribute that effects the specification of one of two sides of a possible (e.g., existence vs. non-existence, length vs. shortness) to occur. He explains that 'attribute' is the genus, 'effects' is a differentia that excludes non-effecting attributes like knowledge and life (but not power), and 'in specification' is a second differentia that excludes power. The intended meaning of specification is giving preponderance (tarjīḥ) to one side over the other.

Correction: The definition refutes these: will is eternal, additional, subsisting, and active in specifying.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Karramiyya thought Allah's will is temporal, like a fleeting desire. Do you ever act as if Allah's will is uncertain or subject to change? Pledge now to recite 'Mā shā'a Allāh' with full conviction before every undertaking.
?
The source says the will 'specifies the possible by some of what is permissible for it.' Your entire existence—your health, wealth, and faith—is a specific possibility chosen by Allah from infinite others. Does that humble you? When you look at your life, do you see it as the product of Allah's precise will or as random chance? Commit to acknowledging His will in every blessing you enjoy today.

Alternative Definition of Will and the Nature of Specification
The author presents an alternative definition of will using a genus-differentia structure, explaining how it excludes other attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the alternative definition of will as an effecting attribute that specifies one of two sides of a possible, and how it distinguishes will from other attributes like power.

Core Idea
Will is the attribute that gives preponderance to one possibility over another, distinct from mere knowledge or power.

Some theologians define will in a slightly different way, focusing on its role in effecting specification. This alternative definition uses a genus-differentia structure to precisely distinguish will from other attributes. We will examine how this definition excludes non-effecting attributes and separates will from power.

Guided Path
1
Read the alternative definition
Read the passage starting with 'wa-baʿḍuhum ʿarrafa al-irādatan bi-annahā: ṣifa tuʾaththiru fī ikhtiṣāṣi aḥadī ṭarafay al-mumkin...' until the end.
2
Understand the genus and differentiae
The definition uses 'attribute' as genus, then 'effects' as first differentia to exclude non-effecting attributes (like knowledge, life), and 'in specification' as second differentia to exclude power.
Power also effects but not in specification; it creates existence.
3
Grasp the concept of tarjīḥ (giving preponderance)
The phrase 'specifying one of the two sides to occur' means giving preponderance (tarjīḥ) to one side over the other. This is the unique role of will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الكلام على هذه الصفة من الجهة الأولى فنقول: الإرادة في اللغة: القصد، وتُرادفها المشيئة ، وهي في اصطلاح علماء الكلام: صفة أزليَّة زائدة على الذات ، قائمة به سبحانه ، تُخَصِّصُ الممكن ببعض ما يجوز عليه ، فقولنا : (صفة) ، كالجنس في التعريف يشمل جميع الصفات، وقولنا: (قديمة) يراد بها الرَّدُّ على نحو الكرَّامية الذين قالوا: إنّ الإرادة صفة حادثة قائمة بذاته تعالى ، تقدَّسَ الله عما يقول المبطلون ، وقولنا : «زائدة على الذات»، يراد به الرَّدُّ على بعض المعتزلة الذين قالوا: إن الإرادة نفس الذات ، وقولنا: «قائمة بذاته تعالى» ، رد على فريقين من المعتزلة ، أولهما الجُبَّائي ومَن ذهب مذهبه من الذين قالوا: إنَّ الإرادة صفة قائمة بغير محلّ ، وثانيهما النَّجَّار ومَن ذهب مذهبه مِن الذين قالوا: إن الإرادة صفة سلبية ، وفسَّروها بأنَّها: عدم كون الفاعل ساهيًا أو مكرها ، وقد علمت فيما سبق أن الصفة السَّلبيَّة لا قيام لها ، لكونها أمرًا عدميًّا ، وقولنا: «تخصص الممكن ببعض ما يجوز عليه»، إشارة إلى التعلق التنجيزي القديم، وهو تخصيص الله تعالى الشيء أزلا بالصفات التي يعلم يوجد عليها في الخارج، وستعرفه مع سائر تعلقات الإرادة في الجهة الثالثة، وبعضهم عرف الإرادة بأنها: صفة تؤثر في اختصاص أحد طرفي الممكن، من وجود أو عدم، أو طول أو قصر ونحوها، بالوقوع بدلا عن مقابله، فقوله: «صفة»، كالجنس في التعريف أنه شامل لجميع الصَّفات، وقوله: «تؤثر»، كالفصل خرج به ما لا يؤثر مِن الصفات ، كالعلم والكلام والسمع والبصر والحياة ونحوها، ما عدا القدرة فإنها لا تخرج بهذا القيد، وقوله: «في اختصاص» ، كفصل ثان خرج به القدرة ، والمراد بتخصيص أحد طرفي الممكن بالوقوع: ترجيح وقوع أحد طرفيه.
As for the discussion on this attribute from the first aspect, we say: al-Irāda (the will) in language is intent (al-qaṣd), and it is synonymous with al-mashī’a (the wish). In the terminology of the scholars of kalām, it is: an eternal attribute (ṣifa azaliyya), additional (zā’ida) to the essence (al-dhāt), subsisting (qā’ima) in Him, may He be exalted, which specifies (tukhaṣṣiṣ) the possible (al-mumkin) by some of what is permissible for it. So our saying: (attribute) – like the genus (al-jins) in the definition – includes all attributes. And our saying: (eternal) intended by it is the refutation of the Karramiyya group who said that the will is a temporal attribute (ṣifa ḥāditha) subsisting in His essence, exalted – exalted is Allah above what the falsifiers say. And our saying: (additional to the essence) intended by it is the refutation of some Mu‘tazila who said that the will is the essence itself. And our saying: (subsisting in His essence, exalted) is a refutation of two groups of the Mu‘tazila: the first is al-Jubbā’ī and those who follow his school who said that the will is an attribute subsisting without a locus; the second is al-Najjār and those who follow his school who said that the will is a negative attribute (ṣifa salbiyya) and interpreted it as: the agent not being negligent or coerced. You have previously learned that the negative attribute has no subsistence, because it is a non–existent matter. And our saying: (which specifies the possible by some of what is permissible for it) is an indication of the eternal determinative specification (al-ta‘alluq al-tanjīzī al-qadīm), which is Allah’s specifying the thing eternally with the attributes upon which He knows it will exist externally. And you will know it along with the other relations of the will in the third aspect. And some defined the will as: an attribute that effects in the specification of one of the two sides of the possible, whether existence or non–existence, or length or shortness and the like, to occur instead of its opposite. So his saying: (attribute) – like the genus in the definition – is that it encompasses all attributes. And his saying: (effects) – like the differentia (al-faṣl) – excludes by it what does not effect of the attributes, such as knowledge, speech, hearing, sight, life and the like, except for power (al-qudra) for it is not excluded by this restriction. And his saying: (in specification) – like a second differentia – excludes by it power (al-qudra). And what is intended by specifying one of the two sides of the possible to occur is: giving preponderance (tarjīḥ) to the occurrence of one of its two sides.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the divine attribute of will (al-irāda). The author begins by giving the linguistic meaning: al-irāda is al-qaṣd (intent), and it is synonymous with al-mashī’a (wish). In kalam terminology, it is defined as an eternal attribute, additional to the essence, subsisting in Allah, that specifies a possible thing by some of what is permissible for it. The author then systematically explains each part of the definition. 'Attribute' is the genus, covering all attributes. 'Eternal' refutes the Karramiyya who held will to be temporal. 'Additional to the essence' refutes the Mu‘tazila who identified will with the essence itself. 'Subsisting in His essence' refutes two Mu‘tazili groups: al-Jubbā’ī and his followers, who said will subsists without a locus, and al-Najjār, who said will is a negative attribute (that the agent is not negligent or coerced). The statement 'specifies the possible by some of what is permissible for it' refers to the eternal determinative specification (al-ta‘alluq al-tanjīzī al-qadīm), i.e., Allah’s eternal determination of what will exist. The author then presents an alternative definition by some scholars: will is an attribute that effects the specification of one of two sides of a possible (e.g., existence vs. non-existence, length vs. shortness) to occur. He explains that 'attribute' is the genus, 'effects' is a differentia that excludes non-effecting attributes like knowledge and life (but not power), and 'in specification' is a second differentia that excludes power. The intended meaning of specification is giving preponderance (tarjīḥ) to one side over the other.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think will is the same as power or knowledge.
Correction: The definition distinguishes will as effecting specification, while knowledge knows without effecting, and power effects creation but not specification.

Checkpoint
In the alternative definition, which attribute is excluded by the second differentia 'in specification'?
A) Knowledge
B) Life
C) Power
D) Speech

Key Takeaway
Will is uniquely defined as the attribute that gives preponderance to one possibility, distinct from knowledge and power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a major decision and weigh two possibilities, do you truly believe that it is Allah's will that gives preponderance to one outcome, or do you act as if your own planning ultimately tips the balance? How can you practically remind yourself of this truth in your next decision?
?
Think of a regret from your past—a choice you wish had gone differently. If Allah's will specifies every possible outcome, what does that mean for your regret? Are you willing to submit to His preponderance and find peace?
?
Is there an area of your life where you desire something but fear it may not happen? How does the knowledge that Allah's will actively effects specification change your dua and reliance? Will you today surrender that desire to His specification, trusting that His choice is best?

Divine Attributes
beginner
4 min
The Six Pairs of Opposing Possibilities
The author enumerates the six pairs of opposing possibilities that relate to creative will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the six pairs of opposing possibilities that are the scope of divine creative will and how they are mutually exclusive.

Core Idea
Divine will selects among six pairs of opposites covering all contingent variation.

This lesson introduces a key concept in Islamic theology: the six pairs of opposing possibilities (al-mumkināt al-mutaqābilāt). These pairs encompass all the ways in which contingent things can differ, and they are the direct objects of God's creative will. Understanding this framework helps clarify how divine predetermination relates to every aspect of creation, from existence to attributes, time, place, direction, and measure.

Guided Path
1
Read and identify the six pairs
Read the passage carefully. The poetic line lists six pairs. Identify each one: existence and non-existence, attributes, times, places, directions, and measures.
The list is given in a verse attributed to reliable transmitters.
2
Understand 'opposing' as mutually exclusive
The author explains that these pairs are opposites because they are mutually exclusive (mutanāfiyāt). For example, the same thing cannot both exist and not exist at the same time.
3
Reflect on theological significance
Consider why theology categorizes possibilities this way. It shows that God's will operates within these categories, selecting one from each pair for every contingent thing.
This connects to divine predestination and the scope of God's power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن الممكنات المتقابلات ستة ، وقد أشار إليها بعضهم في قوله: الممكناتُ المُتَقَابِلَاتُ وُجُودُنَا وَالْعَدَمُ الصِّفَاتُ أَزْمِنَةٌ ، أَمْكِنَةٌ ، جِهَاتٌ كَذَا المَقَادِيرُ ، رَوَى الثَّقَاتُ ومعنى كونها متقابلات أنها متنافياتٌ ؛ فالوجود يقابل العدم، وبالعكس، وبعض الصفات=
And know that the opposing possibles are six, and some of them have alluded to them in his saying: 'The opposing possibles are: our existence and non-existence, attributes, times, places, directions, likewise measures – the trustworthy have narrated.' And the meaning of their being opposites is that they are mutually exclusive; for existence opposes non-existence, and vice versa, and some attributes=
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of the six pairs of opposing possibilities (al-mumkināt al-mutaqābilāt) that are the objects of divine will and power. The author states that there are six such pairs and then quotes a line of poetry that lists them: our existence (i.e., of beings like humans) and non-existence, attributes (i.e., different states or qualities), times, places, directions, and measures (like length or quantity). The poetry attributes this enumeration to reliable transmitters. The author then begins to explain that the meaning of 'opposing' is that these are mutually exclusive: existence and non-existence are opposites, and similarly some attributes are opposites (the text cuts off here). The incomplete sentence suggests the explanation continues on the next page, but the key point is the list of six pairs that cover all possibilities upon which divine will operates in specification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The six pairs are exhaustive of all possible things in existence.
Correction: They are categories of opposition relevant to divine predetermination, not exhaustive of all things.

Checkpoint
According to the poetry cited, which of the following is NOT one of the six opposing possibles?
A) Existence and non-existence
B) Attributes
C) Actions
D) Times

Key Takeaway
The six opposing possibles (existence/non-existence, attributes, times, places, directions, measures) are the categories within which God's creative will selects one opposite, and they are mutually exclusive.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your existence and non-existence are one of the six pairs. How often do you stop to realize that you exist only by God's will, and that He could have chosen non-existence for you? Will this change how you use this day He has given you?
?
Among the six pairs, 'attributes' are listed. Consider a negative attribute you possess—like pride or laziness. How does knowing that God's will selected that specific attribute for you (among all possibilities) make you feel about your responsibility to change it? What will you do about it today?
?
The pairs include time, place, direction, and measure. You are reading this at a specific time, place, and in a certain state. Do you ever feel trapped by your circumstances? How does remembering that your current time, place, and measure are chosen by God's creative will transform your sense of purpose and patience?
